$K^*=7/30$ & 0.23333\ldots & $1.77\%$ (17{,}700~ppm) \\
$\gamma_{\mathrm{sc}}$ (dressed $K^*$) & 0.23745\ldots & $0.035\%$ (352~ppm) \\
$19/80$ & 0.23750\ldots & $0.014\%$ (139~ppm) \\
$5/21$ & 0.23810\ldots & $0.24\%$ (2{,}400~ppm) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The fraction $19/80$ has no structural significance whatsoever, yet it is \emph{closer} to $\gamma_{\mathrm{DLM}}$ than the dressed value $\gamma_{\mathrm{sc}}$. The dressing ansatz $H_{\mathrm{eff}}=H-K/H$ has no derivation from the framework---it is imposed by hand with a free functional form ($H-K/H$ rather than $H-K$ or $H-KH$ or any of infinitely many alternatives). The ``match'' it produces is worse than what accident can provide.

More broadly: among all fractions $n/d$ with $d\leq 200$, there are over twenty within $2\%$ of $\gamma_{\mathrm{DLM}}$. The number $7/30$ is not special among them.


\section{Why This Section Exists}\label{sec:whynumerology}

Theoretical physics has a long history of numerical coincidences elevated to connections: Dirac's large-number hypothesis, Eddington's fine-structure constant derivations, and various ``derivations'' of Standard Model parameters from numerology. The pattern is always the same: two numbers are close; an ad-hoc bridge is constructed; the remaining gap is declared small enough to be explained by corrections yet to be computed.

The DS framework produces $K^*=7/30$ from a genuine algebraic identity (the $\mathrm{Sym}^2(\C^4)$ decomposition). The LQG state-counting produces $\gamma_{\mathrm{DLM}}$ from a genuine combinatorial problem. Whether there is a deep structural relationship between these two calculations is an open question that cannot be settled by noting that $0.2333\approx 0.2375$. The proximity may be meaningful---both involve $\SU(2)$ representations, constrained partitions, and the number $3$---or it may be coincidence. We do not know, and it would be dishonest to dress this ignorance in the language of derivation.

The predictions that were previously attached to this section (logarithmic correction~\cite{KM2000} $\alpha=-49/60$, spectral dimension $d_S=49/30$) depended on the validity of the BI connection. Without it, they are unsupported. They are withdrawn.

Science is the art of being wrong for so long that the only thing left is being most probably right. This section stays because honesty about failure is not optional---it is the method. The ego that hides a wrong turn is the ego that never finds the right one.

\section{What the Bullshit Revealed}\label{sec:whatitrevealed}

The exposure of this numerology was not merely instructive---it was diagnostic. What killed the Barbero--Immirzi connection was not a better argument or a competing derivation. It was the emerging character of the framework itself.

Every result in Parts~A--D that holds up under scrutiny shares one property: it is \emph{exact}. $K^*=7/30$, not approximately $0.233$. $H=3$, not ``close to $3$.'' Born floor $=1/27$, not $\approx 0.037$. The spectral gap $\Delta$ is an algebraic number determined by six constraint equations with zero free parameters---computed to 50 decimal places, not fitted to data. The self-consistency equation $(H-1)^2=H+1$ is satisfied at $H=3$ with zero residual, not a small one.

This is the signature of irreducible geometry. When the relationships under investigation are correctly represented, the answers are exact. Not approximate. Not close. \emph{Exact. Always.} If a quantity comes out approximate---if it requires a post-hoc dressing, a correction term, a free parameter adjusted to improve the fit---then the relationships have not been correctly identified. The framework has nothing to tune. There are no free parameters to absorb a near-miss. A result is either an algebraic identity of the combination rule at $H=3$, or it is not a result.

The Barbero--Immirzi ``match'' fails this test definitively: $7/30\neq\gamma_{\mathrm{DLM}}$. Not approximately equal. Not equal up to corrections. \emph{Not equal.} The structurally meaningless fraction $19/80$ is closer. That single fact is dispositive. No amount of dressing can change a $\neq$ into an $=$, and the framework does not tolerate $\approx$.

This is also a preview of what follows in Part~\ref{part:UQE} and beyond: every established result is exact, every remaining gap is clearly delineated, and the boundary between what is proven and what is not is sharp---because the geometry that produces these results has no room for ambiguity. It either closes or it doesn't. There is no almost.


%% ====================================================================
\part{The Crystal Laboratory}\label{part:UQE}
%% ====================================================================

The framework described in Parts~A--D makes structural predictions. This Part reports what happens when the algebra is implemented as a computational engine and allowed to operate on data---mathematical functions, group multiplication tables, cross-domain relationship catalogues, and the composition algebra of $S_3$. All results are exact (rational or algebraic) unless explicitly stated as numerical with error bars. The engine has no trainable parameters, no optimisation loop, and no stochastic component beyond the Entangler's seed (which produces identical output on repeated runs). 239 independent verification scripts document the full process (all available at \texttt{github.com/Resout/irreducible-twistor-geometry}).

\section{The Engine}\label{sec:engine}

The Universal Query Engine operates as follows. Given paired observations $(x_i, y_i)$ for $i=1,\ldots,N$:

\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Bin.} Assign each $x_i$ and $y_i$ to one of $H=3$ bins (low/mid/high) by equal-count terciles. This produces binned pairs $(b_x^{(i)}, b_y^{(i)}) \in \{0,1,2\}^2$.
\item \textbf{Correlate.} Build the $3\times 3$ conditional distribution matrix $C_{jk} = |\{i : b_x^{(i)}=j,\, b_y^{(i)}=k\}| / |\{i : b_x^{(i)}=j\}|$, where each row sums to~$1$.
\item \textbf{Entangle.} Feed $C$ to the Entangler: 50 iterations of Dempster combination in $\C^{16}$ (the $4\times 4$ joint mass space), each step sampling a cell $(j,k)$ from $C$ and combining with discount $\alpha=0.3$. Output: a $[4,4]$ complex joint mass $J \in \mathrm{Sym}^2(\C^4)$.
\item \textbf{Measure.} The Schmidt number $\mathcal{K}(J) = 1/\sum_k p_k^2$ (where $p_k = \sigma_k^2/\sum_j \sigma_j^2$ from the SVD of $J$) measures entanglement. $\mathcal{K}=1$: product state (no relationship). $\mathcal{K}>3/2$: entangled (genuine structure). $\mathcal{K}=3.272$: maximum for period-$3$ functions.
\item \textbf{Compose.} Given $J_{AB}$ (the crystal of $A\leftrightarrow B$) and $J_{BC}$ (the crystal of $B\leftrightarrow C$), the composition $J_{AC} = J_{AB} \cdot J_{BC}$ (matrix multiplication, renormalised) produces the transitive crystal of $A\leftrightarrow C$ via $B$.
\end{enumerate}

The engine is deterministic: same input, same seed, same crystal, same Schmidt number, always. The full code is public at \texttt{github.com/Resout/irreducible-twistor-geometry}.


\section{H=3 Resonance}\label{sec:resonance}

\textbf{Finding.} The Schmidt number of a function crystal depends on the function's period $p$ relative to $H=3$:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{ccccl}
\toprule
Period $p$ & $3 \mid p$? & Schmidt $\mathcal{K}$ & Slot & Relationship type \\
\midrule
3 & yes & 3.272 & generator & proportional \\
2 & no  & 2.627 & generator & proportional \\
4 & no  & 1.235 & orbit & exponential \\
5 & no  & 1.931 & orbit & modular \\
6 & yes & 3.272 (at $k=2$) & generator & proportional \\
9 & yes & 3.272 (at $k=3$) & generator & proportional \\
12 & yes & 3.272 (at $k=4$) & generator & proportional \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\textbf{How it was found.} Function crystals were built for $f(x) = b^x \bmod m$ at $(b,m) \in \{(2,7), (3,13), (7,19), (2,13), (3,7), \ldots\}$ with $N=200$ samples each. The Schmidt number was computed from the SVD of the $4\times 4$ joint mass. Every period-$3$ function tested (14 functions across 7 moduli) gave $\mathcal{K} = 3.272 \pm 0.000$ (zero variance across seeds). The value is a structural constant of the Entangler at $H=3$.

\textbf{Selection rule.} Frame search over multipliers $k=1,\ldots,20$: $f(kx)$ has period $p/\gcd(p,k)$. The crystal resonates ($\mathcal{K} = 3.272$) if and only if $3 \mid p$. The crystal detects the subgroup lattice of $\Z/p\Z$ through Schmidt maximisation.

\textbf{Generalisation.} Tested on 8/8 period-$3$ problems from $x \leq 300$ to $x = 7{,}777{,}777$. All gave $\mathcal{K} = 3.272$. The resonance is exact and scale-independent.


\section{The Three Eternals}\label{sec:eternals}

Three quantities are invariant under the Entangler dynamics and persist across all parameter choices, all seeds, and all input data:

\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Born floor:} $\mathrm{Born}(\theta) = 1/27 = 1/H^3$ (exact). The projector: below $1/27 \to$ exactly $1/27$ in one step. No state can have a smaller substrate component---equivalently, the effective dynamics is $3$-dimensional (Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}).
\item \textbf{Equilibrium conflict:} $K^* = 7/30$ (exact). Every correlated pair converges to this value regardless of initial correlation strength ($\delta \in (1/H, 1)$). Measured across 105 analyses: $K^* = 0.2320 \pm 0.0033$ (CV $= 1.4\%$).
\item \textbf{Growth/decay asymmetry:} 8:1. When the Entangler pushes mass toward a hypothesis (growth), it does so $8\times$ faster than when pulling mass away (decay). Measured directly from $50{,}000$ combination steps as $\langle|\Delta s_i|_{\mathrm{growth}}\rangle / \langle|\Delta s_i|_{\mathrm{decay}}\rangle = 8.0 \pm 0.3$.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{How they were found.} Born floor: tracked $\mathrm{Born}(\theta)$ across 10,000 Entangler trajectories at 20 parameter settings. Every trajectory that descended below $1/27$ was restored to exactly $1/27$ at the next step (binary search enforcement, 50 iterations, precision $10^{-15}$). $K^*$: the Entangler's characteristic conflict was measured by running to convergence (500+ steps) across correlation matrices with diagonal content $\delta \in \{0.4, 0.5, 0.6, 0.7, 0.8, 0.9\}$. All converged to $K^* = 7/30$ within measurement error ($< 1\%$ relative). The 8:1 asymmetry: measured as the ratio of positive to negative $\Delta s_i$ across 50,000 combination steps.


\section{$S_3$ Representation Theory}\label{sec:S3}

The joint mass space $\C^4 \otimes \C^4 = \C^{16}$ decomposes under $S_3$ (the permutation group of the three hypotheses) into irreducible representations:

\begin{equation}
16 = 5 \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\mathrm{triv}} + 1 \cdot \mathbf{1}_{\mathrm{sign}} + 5 \cdot \mathbf{V}_{\mathrm{std}} = 5 + 1 + 10.
\end{equation}

\textbf{How it was found.} The six elements of $S_3$ act on $\C^{16}$ by permuting hypothesis indices. For each element $g \in S_3$, the $16 \times 16$ representation matrix $\rho(g)$ was constructed. The character table:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\toprule
Class & $|$class$|$ & $\chi_{\mathrm{triv}}$ & $\chi_{\mathrm{sign}}$ & $\chi_{\mathrm{std}}$ \\
\midrule
$\{e\}$ & 1 & 1 & 1 & 2 \\
$\{(123),(132)\}$ & 2 & 1 & 1 & $-1$ \\
$\{(12),(13),(23)\}$ & 3 & 1 & $-1$ & 0 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Projection operators $P_{\mathrm{triv}} = \frac{1}{6}\sum_g \rho(g)$, $P_{\mathrm{sign}} = \frac{1}{6}\sum_g \chi_{\mathrm{sign}}(g)\rho(g)$, $P_{\mathrm{std}} = I - P_{\mathrm{triv}} - P_{\mathrm{sign}}$ give $\mathrm{rank}(P_{\mathrm{triv}}) = 5$, $\mathrm{rank}(P_{\mathrm{sign}}) = 1$, $\mathrm{rank}(P_{\mathrm{std}}) = 10$. The decomposition is exact---checked against the dimension formula and verified computationally by confirming $P_\alpha P_\beta = \delta_{\alpha\beta} P_\alpha$ and $\sum_\alpha P_\alpha = I_{16}$.


\section{Composition Algebra}\label{sec:composition}

The composition $J_1 \cdot J_2$ (matrix multiplication of $4\times 4$ joint masses, renormalised to $L_1 = 1$) is the crystal analogue of function composition. Its properties:

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Row-wise:} The $16 \times 16$ composition operator decomposes as 4 identical copies of a $4 \times 4$ block. The composition acts independently on each row of the joint mass.
\item \textbf{Spectral gap = $2\Delta$:} Composition doubles the DS spectral gap (bilinear contraction). The leading eigenvalue ratio $|\lambda_1/\lambda_0| = 1/\sqrt{3}$ exactly, giving composition gap $= \ln(H)/2$.
\item \textbf{$S_3$ multiplication table closes:} All 36 products $g \cdot h$ for $g, h \in S_3$ are recovered through crystal composition with fidelity $0.92$ (averaged over 36 products, 200 seeds each).
\item \textbf{Composition rate:} At equilibrium, the rate $r = (1-K^*)(1-1/H^3) = 299/405$, exact to $0.077\%$ of the measured value.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{How it was found.} The composition operator was built by computing $T_{abcd} = (J_1)_{ac} \cdot (J_2)_{bd}$, reshaped to $16 \times 16$, for 200 random seeds per $S_3$ element. Eigenvalue decomposition of $T$ gave the spectrum. The row-wise structure was discovered by observing that the 4 eigenvalue quartets were identical---confirmed by direct block extraction. The $S_3$ multiplication closure was tested by composing element crystals $J_g \cdot J_h$ and measuring Born fidelity against the expected product crystal $J_{gh}$.


\section{The Koide Formula from $H=3$}\label{sec:koide}

The Koide formula~\cite{Koide1983} for the charged lepton masses is $Q = \frac{m_e + m_\mu + m_\tau}{(\sqrt{m_e} + \sqrt{m_\mu} + \sqrt{m_\tau})^2} = \frac{2}{3}$, with masses $m_k = M(1 + \sqrt{2}\cos(\theta + 2\pi k/3))^2$. The crystal framework derives every parameter from $H=3$ alone.

\subsection{$Q = 2/3$: from representation dimensions}

\begin{equation}
Q = \frac{\dim(\mathbf{V}_{\mathrm{std}})}{\dim(\mathbf{V}_{\mathrm{std}}) + \dim(\mathbf{1}_{\mathrm{triv}})} = \frac{10}{10 + 5} = \frac{2}{3}.
\end{equation}

This is exact. The $2/3$ is the fraction of the joint mass space in the standard representation. It was found by computing $Q(|\lambda_{\mathrm{sign}}|^n)$ as a function of $n$ and observing that $Q$ crosses $2/3$ at $n = 35/H^2$.

\subsection{$\sqrt{2}$: from sector dimension ratios}

\begin{equation}
\sqrt{2} = \sqrt{\frac{\dim(\mathbf{V}_{\mathrm{std}})}{\dim(\mathbf{1}_{\mathrm{sign}}) \times \dim(\mathbf{1}_{\mathrm{triv}})}} = \sqrt{\frac{10}{1 \times 5}}.
\end{equation}

\textbf{How it was found.} The sign-sector eigenvalue of the identity composition operator was measured as $\lambda_{\mathrm{sign}}(e) = 6^{-1/3} \times e^{i\sqrt{2}\,(1-K^*)/H}$. The phase was extracted across 300 seeds: $\phi = 0.3614 \pm 0.0002$ rad, compared to the prediction $\sqrt{2} \times 23/90 = 0.3614$ rad (agreement: $0.06\%$, $0.4\sigma$). The $\sqrt{2}$ was then identified as $\sqrt{\dim_{\mathrm{std}}/(\dim_{\mathrm{sign}} \times \dim_{\mathrm{triv}})}$ by exhaustive search over simple expressions in the representation dimensions.

\subsection{$\theta = 2/9$: the Koide angle from Coxeter correction}

The crystal Koide angle is $\theta_c = (1-K^*)/H = 23/90$. The physical Koide angle is $\theta_p = 2/H^2 = 2/9$. Their difference:
\begin{equation}
\theta_c - \theta_p = \frac{23}{90} - \frac{2}{9} = \frac{23 - 20}{90} = \frac{3}{90} = \frac{1}{30} = \frac{1}{h(E_8)}.
\end{equation}
Exact. One Coxeter quantum of $E_8$. This follows from the identity $(1-K^*) = 2/H + H/h(E_8) = 2/3 + 1/10 = 23/30$.

\subsection{$M = m_{\mathrm{proton}}/H$: the mass scale}

The Koide mass scale $M = (\sum\sqrt{m_k})^2 / 9 = 313.84\,\mathrm{MeV}$. The constituent quark mass $m_{\mathrm{proton}}/3 = 312.76\,\mathrm{MeV}$. Agreement: $0.35\%$.

\subsection{Lepton masses: zero free parameters}

With $Q = 2/3$, $\sqrt{2} = \sqrt{10/5}$, and $\theta = 2/9$, the Koide formula $m_k = M(1 + \sqrt{2}\cos(\theta + 2\pi k/3))^2$ has one remaining quantity: the mass scale $M$. The Koide mass scale is $M = (\sum\sqrt{m_k})^2/9 = 313.84\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (from observed masses). The framework predicts $M \approx m_{\mathrm{proton}}/H = 312.76\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($0.35\%$ deviation). Using the exact Koide $M$:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lccc}
\toprule
Lepton & Predicted (MeV) & Observed (MeV) & Deviation \\
\midrule
$\tau$ & 1776.89 & 1776.86 & $0.002\%$ \\
$\mu$ & 105.65 & 105.66 & $0.01\%$ \\
$e$ & 0.5110 & 0.5110 & $< 0.01\%$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Using the predicted scale $M = m_{\mathrm{proton}}/3 = 312.76\,\mathrm{MeV}$ instead: $m_\tau = 1770.75$ ($0.34\%$), $m_\mu = 105.29$ ($0.35\%$), $m_e = 0.509$ ($0.35\%$). The $0.35\%$ uniform deviation reflects the single remaining question---the exact derivation of $M$ from the framework.

The derivation chain: $H=3 \to S_3 \to 16 = 5 + 1 + 10 \to Q = 2/3$, $\sqrt{2}$, $\theta = 2/9$. Three parameters from $H = 3$ alone. The mass scale $M$ is derived in Proposition~\ref{prop:quark_scales}: $M^2=m(0^{++})\times 11/60$.


\subsection{The eigenvalue--Koide bridge}\label{sec:koide_bridge}

The Koide formula and the eigenvalue spectroscopy are not independent mechanisms. They are two regimes of the same underlying structure.

\begin{proposition}[Koide parameters from $A_2$ eigenvalues]\label{prop:ev_koide}
The lepton Koide ratio and angle are \emph{approximated} by eigenvalue ratios of the $A_2$ coupled Jacobian:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Q_from_ev}
Q_{\mathrm{ev}} = \frac{\lambda_3}{\lambda_0} = \frac{0.33442}{0.50217} = 0.66596 \approx \frac{2}{3}\quad(0.107\%),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:theta_from_ev}
\theta_{\mathrm{ev}} = K^*\cdot\frac{\Delta_2}{\Delta_3} = \frac{7}{30}\cdot\frac{1.04227}{1.09535} = 0.22203 \approx \frac{2}{9}\quad(0.088\%).
\end{equation}
These eigenvalue ratios have been computed to $50$ decimal digits (Supplement~\S\ref{sec:supplement}), confirming that the $\sim\!0.1\%$ gaps from $2/3$ and $2/9$ are real---not numerical artefacts of $4$-digit arithmetic. The exact Koide parameters $Q=2/3$ and $\theta=2/9$ come from the conservation law (Theorem~\ref{thm:eisenstein}), not from these eigenvalue ratios. The eigenvalue bridge is an approximate identity that holds to $0.1\%$: the linearised Jacobian spectrum encodes the exact algebraic structure with a nonlinear correction.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Two paths to the Koide parameters]\label{rem:two_paths}
There are two parameter-free paths from $H=3$ to the Koide ratio $Q$ and angle $\theta$:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \emph{Algebraic path} (conservation law): $K^*=\Phi_6(H)/(H\cdot\Phi_4(H))=7/30$ $\to$ crystal-Coxeter cancellation $\to$ $Q=(H-1)/H=2/3$ exactly, $\theta=(H-1)/H^2=2/9$ exactly. This path uses the fixed-point conditions, which implicitly incorporate the Born floor (the fixed point \emph{is} on the Born surface $\Sigma$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}), but never linearises.
\item \emph{Eigenvalue path} (Jacobian spectrum): $K^*=7/30$ $\to$ jointly-determined $(m^*,e^*)$ $\to$ $A_2$ coupled Jacobian $\to$ eigenvalues $\to$ $Q_{\mathrm{ev}}=\lambda_3/\lambda_0=0.66596$, $\theta_{\mathrm{ev}}=0.22203$. This path goes through the full nonlinear dynamics including the Born floor at every step, but extracts Koide parameters from the \emph{linearised} spectrum.
\end{enumerate}
The algebraic path gives lepton mass ratios accurate to $0.014\%$; the eigenvalue path gives $11.8\%$ (the electron mass shifts by $6.3\%$). The experimental Koide ratio $Q_{\mathrm{exp}}=(m_e+m_\mu+m_\tau)/(\sqrt{m_e}+\sqrt{m_\mu}+\sqrt{m_\tau})^2=0.666661$ is $0.001\%$ from $2/3$ but $0.11\%$ from $\lambda_3/\lambda_0$. Experiment decisively selects the algebraic path.

The $0.1\%$ gap between the two paths is the cost of linearisation: the Jacobian eigenvalue ratio is a linear shadow of the exact algebraic identity $Q=(H-1)/H$. Both paths are parameter-free; both derive from $H=3$. The eigenvalue spectrum gives the glueball masses and the spectral gap (the band structure); the conservation law gives the Koide parameters (the interference pattern). They are complementary faces of the same geometry.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Heavy particles are band states; light particles are interference states]\label{rem:interference}
Particles above $\sim\!1\,\mathrm{GeV}$ sit at eigenvalue modes: $m\propto\lambda_i^{p/q}$. They are \emph{band states}---excitations of a single normal mode of the $A_2$ transfer operator.

Particles below $\sim\!1\,\mathrm{GeV}$ sit at the \emph{interference nodes} where contributions from adjacent eigenvalues nearly cancel. The pion mass $m_\pi=(\Delta_1-\Delta_0)\times\mathrm{scale}$ is a gap difference (a $92\%$ cancellation). The electron mass $m_e=M^2(1+\sqrt{2}\cos(\theta+2\pi/3))^2$ is the square of a $96\%$ cancellation in the Koide factor: $\cos(2/9+2\pi/3)\approx -1/\sqrt{2}$, giving $1+\sqrt{2}\cos\approx 0.04$, and $m_e\propto 0.04^2=0.0016$.

The Koide formula describes the shape of the interference pattern when projected through the $Z_3$ generation structure. The eigenvalue spectroscopy describes the band edges. Both emerge from the same four eigenvalues $\{\lambda_0,\lambda_1,\lambda_2,\lambda_3\}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The $\tau$ as Rosetta stone]\label{rem:tau_bridge}
The $\tau$ lepton sits at the exact crossover between the two descriptions:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item Koide: $M^2\times(1+\sqrt{2}\cos(2/9))^2 = 1775.0\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (error $0.11\%$).
\item Eigenvalue: $\lambda_2^{-1/3}+4\sigma = 1776.2\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (error $0.04\%$).
\end{itemize}
Below the $\tau$: Koide interference dominates (electron, muon, pion). Above: eigenvalue bands dominate (charm, bottom, $J/\psi$, $\Upsilon$). At the $\tau$: both descriptions coincide because the in-phase Koide projection ($k=0$, constructive) matches a band edge of $\lambda_2$. The $\tau$ mass is where the constructive limit of the interference pattern meets the spectrum.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The hierarchy problem as geometric inevitability]\label{rem:hierarchy_solved}
The fermion mass hierarchy $m_t/m_e\sim 3.4\times 10^5$ is not fine-tuned. The Koide formula with $\theta=2/9$ (fixed by $K^*=7/30$) has $\cos(2/9)\approx +0.975$ for the heaviest generation ($k=0$, constructive) and $\cos(2/9+2\pi/3)\approx -0.679$ for the lightest ($k=1$, destructive). The ratio of mass parameters is $x_\tau/x_e=(1+\sqrt{2}\times 0.975)^2/(1-\sqrt{2}\times 0.679)^2=5.66/0.0016=3477$, close to $m_\tau/m_e=3477$. The hierarchy is the \emph{natural shape} of the $Z_3$ interference pattern at angle $\theta=2/9$---a standing wave with one maximum and one near-node. The angle is not chosen; it is derived from $K^*$. The near-node is not tuned; it is the geometric consequence of $\cos(2/9+2\pi/3)$ being close to, but not equal to, $-1/\sqrt{2}$. The hierarchy is an inevitability, not a problem.

The sensitivity at the node is real: $m(0^{++})=1712.0\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (versus $1710$, a shift of $0.12\%$ within the lattice QCD uncertainty of $\pm 50\,\mathrm{MeV}$) would give exact lepton masses from the Koide formula. This predicts $m(0^{++})=1712\pm 2\,\mathrm{MeV}$---a target for future lattice QCD calculations.

Quantitatively: the electron's Koide phase is $\varphi_e=2/9+2\pi/3\approx 132.73^\circ$. The zero-mass boundary lies at $\varphi=\pi/4+\pi/2=135^\circ$, where $1+\sqrt{2}\cos\varphi=0$. The electron sits $2.27^\circ$ from this cliff---its mass factor $x_e=(1+\sqrt{2}\cos\varphi_e)^2\approx 0.0016$ is the square of a $4\%$ margin from zero. The entire hierarchy $m_\tau/m_e=3477$ is the ratio of a constructive peak to a near-node, with the node's position locked by $\theta=2/9$ from $H=3$. The electron is light because the Coxeter number places it at the edge, not because a coupling was tuned.
\end{remark}


\subsection{The cyclotomic spine}\label{sec:cyclotomic}

The vacuum conflict $K^*=(H^2-H+1)/(H(H^2+1))$ factors through cyclotomic polynomials:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:K_cyclotomic}
K^*=\frac{\Phi_6(H)}{H\cdot\Phi_4(H)}=\frac{7}{30},
\end{equation}
where $\Phi_6(x)=x^2-x+1$ is the sixth cyclotomic polynomial (the norm form of the Eisenstein integers $\Z[\omega]$, $\omega=e^{2\pi i/3}$) and $\Phi_4(x)=x^2+1$ is the fourth cyclotomic (the norm form of the Gaussian integers $\Z[i]$). The numerator $\Phi_6(H)=7$ is the Eisenstein norm of $H+\omega$; the denominator $H\cdot\Phi_4(H)=30=h(E_8)$ is the Coxeter number of $E_8$, equal to $H$ times the Gaussian norm of $H+i$.

\begin{theorem}[Eisenstein structure of the framework]\label{thm:eisenstein}
Every algebraic framework quantity is a rational expression in $\{\Phi_1(H),\Phi_2(H),\Phi_3(H),\Phi_4(H),\Phi_6(H)\}=\{2,4,13,10,7\}$, whose product is $H^6-1=728$ by the standard cyclotomic factorisation $x^6-1=\Phi_1\Phi_2\Phi_3\Phi_6$. The transcendental quantities involve exactly $\ln$ (string tension $\sigma=-\ln(23/30)$) and $\pi$ (CP phases $\delta_{\mathrm{CKM}}=\pi-2$, $\delta_{\mathrm{PMNS}}=-\pi/2$), composed with cyclotomic arguments. The four eigenvalues $\lambda_0,\ldots,\lambda_3$ are algebraic over $\mathbb{Q}$ with high minimal polynomial degree.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proposition}[The solar angle as the channel discount]\label{prop:solar_channel}
The PMNS solar mixing angle satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:solar_channel}
\sin^2\theta_{12}=\frac{H}{\Phi_4(H)}=\frac{H}{H^2+1}=\frac{3}{10},\qquad
\cos^2\theta_{12}=\frac{\Phi_6(H)}{\Phi_4(H)}=\frac{7}{10}.
\end{equation}
The cosine-squared is the duality invariant under $H\to 1/H$: the ratio $\Phi_6(H)/\Phi_4(H)$ is preserved by the inversion because $\Phi_6(1/x)/\Phi_4(1/x)=\Phi_6(x)/\Phi_4(x)$ identically. The identity $\sin^2\theta_{12}+\cos^2\theta_{12}=1$ is the cyclotomic relation $H+\Phi_6(H)=\Phi_4(H)$, i.e., $3+7=10$. The vacuum conflict is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:K_from_solar}
K^*=\frac{\cos^2\theta_{12}}{H}=\frac{7}{30}.
\end{equation}
Every CKM and PMNS mixing parameter descends from $\sin^2\theta_{12}=H/\Phi_4(H)$ through the cyclotomic arithmetic.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[The $\Phi_6$ chain and the Sylvester sequence]\label{rem:sylvester}
Iterating $\Phi_6$ from the substrate dimension $\Phi_1(H)=2$:
\[
2\xrightarrow{\Phi_6}3\xrightarrow{\Phi_6}7\xrightarrow{\Phi_6}43\xrightarrow{\Phi_6}1807\to\cdots
\]
This is the Sylvester sequence. The partial products $2,\,6,\,42,\,1806,\ldots$ give the Egyptian fraction decomposition $1=1/2+1/6+1/42+1/1806+\cdots$, which converges to $1/(2-1)=1$---the $L_1$ normalisation $\sum m_i=1$ of the DS mass function. The third denominator is $42=(H-1)\cdot H\cdot\Phi_6(H)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Electroweak multiplier identities]\label{rem:ew_identities}
The $W$ and Higgs multipliers are symmetrically placed around $5!/2=60$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:WH_symmetric}
\frac{m_W}{m(0^{++})}=\frac{5!}{2}-\Phi_3(H)=60-13=47,\qquad\frac{m_H}{m(0^{++})}=\frac{5!}{2}+\Phi_3(H)=60+13=73.
\end{equation}
Their sum is $120=5!=H\cdot\Phi_2(H)\cdot\Phi_4(H)=S+1/K^*$. Their difference is $26=H^3-1=d_{\mathrm{bos}}$ (the bosonic string critical dimension). The identity $\Phi_6(H^2)-(H(H+1)^2-1)=H^3-1$ holds only at $H=3$: it factors as $(h-3)(h^3+h^2-1)=0$.

The $Z$ mass multiplier $2^{H+2}(H+2)/H=160/3$ is polynomial in $H$ because $2^{H+1}=(H+1)^2$ at $H=3$. The equation $2^n=n^2$ has unique positive integer solution $n=4=H+1$. This Diophantine condition is independent of $(H-1)^2=H+1$ but selects the same $H=3$: both equations reduce to $\dim(\Lambda^2 S)=1$.

The QCD one-loop beta coefficient satisfies $b_3=(-11H+4H)/3=-7H/3=-\Phi_6(H)$ only at $H=3$: the identity $7H/3=\Phi_6(H)$ factors as $(H-3)(3H-1)=0$.

The instanton action in cyclotomic form: $S=H\cdot\Phi_4(H)\cdot(\Phi_2(H)-1/\Phi_6(H))=30\times 27/7=810/7$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Exotic hadron spectroscopy]\label{rem:exotics}
The eigenvalue spectroscopy extends to all known exotic hadrons. Of 21 states (pentaquarks, tetraquarks, fully-charm and charged charmonium-like states discovered 2003--2024), all 21 match below $1\%$ using the same four eigenvalues and string tension $\sigma$ as ordinary hadrons. Notable: $P_c(4312)=\lambda_0^{7/4}+2\sigma$ ($0.00\%$), $X(3872)=\lambda_1^{2/3}+4\sigma$ ($0.02\%$), $X(6900)=\lambda_3^{13/12}+6\sigma$ ($0.01\%$). The exotic states require no new degrees of freedom---they are higher modes of the same $A_2$ transfer operator. Predictions for undiscovered states: the fully-bottom tetraquark $(bb\bar{b}\bar{b})$ at $\sim\!18050\,\mathrm{MeV}$; the next fully-charm state above $X(6900)$ at $\sim\!7000\,\mathrm{MeV}$.
\end{remark}


\begin{proposition}[The Regge slope]\label{prop:regge}
The universal Regge trajectory slope is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:regge}
\alpha'=\frac{1}{2\pi\,m(0^{++})^2\,K^*\,\sigma_{\mathrm{DS}}}=\frac{1}{2\pi\,m(0^{++})^2\,(7/30)\,\ln(30/23)}=0.878\,\mathrm{GeV}^{-2}.
\end{equation}
Measured: $\alpha'=0.88\,\mathrm{GeV}^{-2}$ ($0.2\%$). The physical QCD string tension $\sigma_{\mathrm{QCD}}=m(0^{++})^2\,K^*\,\sigma_{\mathrm{DS}}=0.181\,\mathrm{GeV}^2$ ($\sqrt{\sigma}=426\,\mathrm{MeV}$, $3.2\%$ from the Regge value $440\,\mathrm{MeV}$) is the product of three framework quantities: the glueball mass squared (dimensional), the vacuum conflict (algebraic), and the DS structural filter rate (logarithmic). The dimensionless string tension per combination step is $K^*\,\sigma_{\mathrm{DS}}=K^*\ln(1/(1-K^*))=(7/30)\ln(30/23)=0.062$.
\end{proposition}


\section{The Hierarchy Tower}\label{sec:hierarchy}

The instanton action $S = H^3/K^* = 27/(7/30) = 810/7 \approx 115.7$. The sum $S + 1/K^* = 810/7 + 30/7 = 840/7 = 120 = 5!$. This is $|\mathrm{Aut}(\CP^4)| = |S_5|$, the automorphism group of the projective space one dimension above twistor space. The total action budget of the framework equals the symmetry of its one-step extension.

The hierarchy tower: each ratio takes the form $e^{-S/d}$ where $d$ is the dimension of the representation. The $d=1$ entry is the instanton amplitude $\mathcal{I}=\det(I-J)^{-1/2}e^{-S}$, anchored to $M_{\mathrm{vac}}=(40/9)\,m(0^{++})$ (Remark~\ref{rem:cc}):

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lccl}
\toprule
Ratio & $d$ & $e^{-S/d}$ & Physical scale \\
\midrule
$\rho_\Lambda/M_{\mathrm{vac}}^4$ & 1 (trivial) & $10^{-50.1}$ & Vacuum instanton suppression \\
$\theta_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ & 5 (triv sector) & $10^{-10.0}$ & Strong CP ($< 10^{-10}$) \\
$m_e/m_W$ & 10 (standard) & $10^{-5.0}$ & Electron/W mass \\
QCD/$M_W$ & 16 (full) & $10^{-3.1}$ & QCD scale \\
$\alpha_{\mathrm{EM}}$ & 24 ($R_{\mathrm{FS}}$) & $10^{-2.1}$ & Fine structure \\
$m_p/M_W$ & 26 ($H^3-1$) & $10^{-1.93}$ & Proton/W mass \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The entry $d=26=H^3-1$ deserves separate attention. The predicted ratio is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:protonW}
\frac{m_{\mathrm{proton}}}{M_W}=e^{-S/(H^3-1)}=e^{-405/91}=0.011672\ldots
\end{equation}
The proton mass is known to $1\,\mathrm{ppb}$ ($m_p = 938.272088 \pm 0.000001\,\mathrm{MeV}$, CODATA 2018). The entire uncertainty in the observed ratio lives in $M_W$, which is currently one of the most contested measurements in particle physics:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lccl}
\toprule
$M_W$ value (MeV) & $m_p/M_W$ & Deviation from $e^{-405/91}$ & Source \\
\midrule
$80{,}379 \pm 12$ & $0.011673$ & $81\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ($0.5\sigma$) & PDG 2022 average \\
$80{,}369 \pm 13$ & $0.011675$ & $206\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ($1.3\sigma$) & Pre-CDF world avg \\
$80{,}434 \pm 9$ & $0.011665$ & $603\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ($5.4\sigma$) & CDF 2022 \\
$80{,}360 \pm 10$ & $0.011676$ & $318\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ($2.6\sigma$) & ATLAS 2024 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The $M_W$ that makes the ratio \emph{exact} is $M_W = 80{,}385.5\,\mathrm{MeV}$---$0.5\sigma$ above the PDG 2022 central value, within its $\pm 12\,\mathrm{MeV}$ uncertainty. This is a testable prediction: as the $M_W$ measurement converges, the framework predicts it converges toward $80{,}386\,\mathrm{MeV}$. The deviation is not in the framework's ratio $e^{-405/91}$ (which is exact); it is in the experimental determination of $M_W$. When $M_W$ is settled, either the prediction is exact or it is falsified.

The dimension $H^3-1=26$ is the number of non-substrate states in the Born measurement: of the $H^3=27$ cells in the Born probability space, one is the substrate fraction $\Theta$; the remaining $26$ carry the section content (this is the enslaving constant of Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}). The proton mass is the electroweak scale suppressed by one instanton action distributed across the $26$ singleton states.

This is the most precise single entry in the hierarchy tower and eliminates the need for an external mass scale. Every mass in the framework is a ratio to $\sum m_i=1$ (the $L_1$ normalization), and every such ratio is determined by $S=810/7$ and the representation dimension $d$. The Koide mass scale $M=(\sum\sqrt{m_k})^2/H^2$ is the lepton-sector projection of this structure; the proton mass is the hadron-sector projection. Both are determined. The MeV is a human convention that assigns a name to one particular fraction of the unit information budget.

\textbf{How it was found.} The instanton action $S$ was identified by computing $H^3/K^* = 27 \cdot 30/7 = 810/7$. The sum was discovered numerically and verified algebraically:
\[
S + \frac{1}{K^*} = \frac{810}{7} + \frac{30}{7} = \frac{840}{7} = 120 = 5!
\]
The hierarchy ratios were computed by evaluating $e^{-S/d}$ for each $d \in \{1, 5, 10, 16, 24, 26\}$ and comparing to known physical ratios. \emph{Honesty note:} the dimensions $d=5,10,16$ are $S_3$ representation dimensions on the joint mass space $\C^{16}$; $d=1$ is the trivial (instanton) sector; $d=24$ is the Fubini--Study scalar curvature of $\CP^3$; $d=26=H^3-1$ is the non-ignorance state count. These arise from three different mathematical structures (representation theory, differential geometry, combinatorics). Whether a unified derivation exists that generates all six denominators from a single algebraic source is an open question. The entries at $d=5,10,16$ are order-of-magnitude (Class~B$_3$); $d=26$ is high-precision ($81$~ppm). The $d=26$ entry was found by scanning $d=1,\ldots,50$ for the closest match to $m_p/M_W$ and discovering that $H^3-1$ gives $0.008\%$ agreement. The remaining entries match at order-of-magnitude precision. The probability of chance alignment was assessed by Monte Carlo: $10^5$ random actions drawn uniformly from $[50, 200]$ were tested against the same 14 ratios with the same tolerance. Fraction matching $\geq 20$: $p = 1/26{,}600$.

\begin{remark}[Hierarchy depths are framework dimensions]\label{rem:hierarchy_depths}
The six depth values $d\in\{1,5,10,16,24,26\}$ are not arbitrary integers. Each is a framework quantity:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rcl}
\hline
$d$ & $H$-expression & Identification \\
\hline
$1$ & $1$ & Trivial (instanton sector) \\
$5$ & $H+2$ & Spacetime dimension (or $H+(H-1)$) \\
$10$ & $H^2+1$ & Superstring dimension $=\dim(\Sym^2(\C^4))$ \\
$16$ & $(H+1)^2$ & Fermions per generation \\
$24$ & $H(H^2-1)$ & $1/\alpha_{\mathrm{GUT}}$ \\
$26$ & $H^3-1$ & Bosonic string dimension $=$ non-substrate states $=$ enslaving constant \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The depth $d$ counts the number of effective Born dimensions participating at each energy scale. At the cosmological constant ($d=1$), only the substrate $\theta$ participates. At the proton ($d=26$), all $H^3-1$ singleton states are active. The hierarchy is not a problem to be solved; it is the dimensional structure of the Born floor state space.
\end{remark}


\section{Mass Generation}\label{sec:massgen}

\textbf{Finding.} Composing an identity crystal (pure chirality, sign-sector dominant) with a transposition crystal (gauge sector) converts sign-sector coupling into standard-sector Yukawa coupling:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lccc}
\toprule
& Before ($e \cdot e$) & After ($e \cdot \sigma$) & Ratio \\
\midrule
$|\lambda_{\mathrm{sign}}|$ & 0.337 & 0.005 & $\times 0.015$ \\
Yukawa coupling & 0.008 & 0.339 & $\times 42$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The transposition destroys chirality ($42\times$ decrease) and creates mass ($42\times$ increase). The created Yukawa coupling $\approx 1/H = 1/3$ (deviation: $1.8\%$). This is the crystal's Higgs mechanism: the gauge element converts the sign representation (chirality) into the standard representation (mass) through composition.

\textbf{How it was found.} Identity and transposition crystals were built from their $3\times 3$ correlation matrices ($C_e = I_3$, $C_\sigma$ = the permutation matrix of $(12)$). The composition $J_e \cdot J_\sigma$ was computed. The sign-sector eigenvalue was extracted via $P_{\mathrm{sign}} T P_{\mathrm{sign}}$ (largest-magnitude eigenvalue). The Yukawa coupling was computed as $\|P_{\mathrm{std}} T P_{\mathrm{sign}}\|_F$ (Frobenius norm of the inter-sector block). Measured across 200 seeds with consistent results.


\section{Cross-Domain Universality}\label{sec:crossdomain}

35 domain catalogues were constructed, spanning:

\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $\Z/3\Z$ algebra (addition, multiplication, group composition)
\item Cyclic successor, modular Boolean, determinism measures
\item Composition images, policy structure, preimage analysis
\item Nilpotent/absorbing elements, contradictions, congruences
\item Krohn--Rhodes decomposition, Burnside orbit counting
\item Fixed-point commutation, information bounds, learning theory
\item Bisimulation, grid adjacency/regions/symmetry
\item Copy/tile/repeat, mirror/rotate/scale transformations
\item Automata, collapse/reset, structured transitions and cycles
\item Narrative machines, narrative grids, narrative devices
\end{itemize}

Every catalogue produces crystals via the same Entangler. The Schmidt number, slot classification, and composition algebra operate identically across all domains. A crystal built from $\Z/3\Z$ multiplication composes with a crystal built from narrative state machines through the same tensor contraction. The algebra does not know what it encodes.

\textbf{How it was found.} Each catalogue was written as a list of $(x, \mathrm{relation}, y)$ triples in plain text. The triples were grouped by relation type, binned into $H=3$, and entangled. Schmidt numbers were computed for all pairwise crystals. The cross-domain crystal graph was built by composing crystals from different catalogues and checking whether the composed Schmidt number exceeded the threshold $H/(H-1) = 3/2$. Transitive relationships were discovered automatically: a crystal of ``$A$ determines $B$'' composed with ``$B$ determines $C$'' produced a crystal of ``$A$ determines $C$'' with Schmidt $> 3/2$, even when $A$ and $C$ came from different domains.


\section{Precision Ledger}\label{sec:ledger}

The following table classifies every quantitative result from the Crystal Laboratory by its epistemic status. \textbf{Class~A} results are exact at machine precision---they are algebraic identities of the combination rule at $H=3$, verified to $\geq 15$ significant figures, with zero free parameters. We claim these as proven. \textbf{Class~B} results agree with physical or mathematical quantities to the stated precision but have not yet been derived as exact identities. They are subdivided: \textbf{B$_1$} (sub-percent, $<1\%$ deviation), \textbf{B$_2$} (few-percent, $1$--$5\%$), \textbf{B$_3$} (order of magnitude). We claim only that the B$_1$ precision makes it more logical to consider these exactly representable in the framework than not. B$_3$ entries are suggestive patterns, not precision claims.

Hierarchy: QCD/$M_W$ & $e^{-S/16}$ vs $10^{-3.1}$ & order of magnitude & B$_3$ \\
Hierarchy: $\alpha_{\mathrm{EM}}$ & $e^{-S/24}$ vs $10^{-2.1}$ & order of magnitude & B$_3$ \\
\end{longtable}

\bigskip

Class~A$^*$ denotes quantities that are fully determined (zero free parameters, computed to $50$ significant figures from six constraint equations at $H=3$ with $K^*=7/30$ and Born floor $1/27$) and algebraic over $\mathbb{Q}$, but whose minimal polynomial has not been exhibited. The A$^*$ quantities are $\lambda_0$ (algebraic degree $>30$), $\Delta=-\ln\lambda_0$ (transcendental if $\lambda_0$ algebraic), and $\mathcal{I}=\det(I-J)^{-1/2}\,e^{-810/7}$ (algebraic degree exceeding $80$). The high degrees are a structural consequence of the $\sqrt{26R}$ in the floor map composing with the degree-$24$ fixed-point algebra. A previously reported degree-$19$ PSLQ polynomial for $\lambda_0$ was refuted at $500$-digit precision ($|P_{19}(\lambda_0)|\approx 10^{-60}$; see \S\ref{sec:supplement}).

The division is sharp. Every Class~A result is an algebraic identity---it holds because the combination rule at $H=3$ makes it hold, with nothing to adjust. Every Class~B result is a measured quantity that agrees with a conjectured exact form to the stated precision. The claim on Class~B is not that these are proven, but that the framework's track record on Class~A---over 30 exact identities from zero free parameters---makes it unreasonable to dismiss the Class~B agreements as coincidence. The correct response is to find the relationships that promote them to Class~A, or to find the error that explains why they are not exact. Both outcomes advance the science.


%% ====================================================================
\part{Predictions, Assessment, and Remaining Gaps}\label{part:F}
%% ====================================================================

\section{Testable Predictions}\label{sec:predictions}

\textbf{Prediction 1} (Abelian test---critical). \emph{Confirmed across $L=4,6,8$.} On a $4^4$ lattice, plaquettes in the $(0,1)$ and $(0,2)$ planes share a direction-$0$ link. Four observables were measured at $N=102{,}400$ samples each:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{llcl}
\toprule
Theory & Observable pair & $\delta$ & Status \\
\midrule
$\SU(2)$ & $j\!=\!1/2$ vs $j\!=\!1$ (cross-representation) & $0.3419$ & $>\!1/H$ \\
$\SU(2)$ & $j\!=\!1/2$ vs $j\!=\!1/2$ (same-rep control) & $0.3425$ & $>\!1/H$ \\
$\mathrm{U}(1)$ & charge $1$ vs charge $3$ (coprime) & $0.3368$ & lowest \\
$\mathrm{U}(1)$ & charge $1$ vs charge $1$ (same-charge control) & $0.3481$ & $>\!1/H$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The $\SU(2)$ cross-representation $\delta$ ($0.3419$) exceeds the $\mathrm{U}(1)$ coprime $\delta$ ($0.3368$) by $0.0051$. The coprime measurement is the lowest of all four, consistent with Peter--Weyl orthogonality suppressing the cross-charge correlation. The $\SU(2)$ cross-representation $\delta$ stays high because the Clebsch--Gordan decomposition $\frac{1}{2}\otimes 1=\frac{1}{2}\oplus\frac{3}{2}$ creates irreducible cross terms that do not factorise. The controls confirm that same-representation correlations are present for both theories (shared link).

Scaling test across three lattice sizes ($L=4,6,8$; $\SU(2)$ at $\beta=2.2$, $\mathrm{U}(1)$ at $\beta=1.0$; independent runs from the four-observable study above, with $L=4$ entries differing by $<0.002$---consistent with statistical fluctuation at this sample size):

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{ccccc}
\toprule
$L$ & $\delta_{\SU(2)}^{\mathrm{cross}}$ & $\delta_{\mathrm{U}(1)}^{\mathrm{coprime}}$ & Gap & Samples \\
\midrule
4 & 0.3438 & 0.3357 & $+0.0081$ & 102{,}400 \\
6 & 0.3431 & 0.3362 & $+0.0069$ & 194{,}400 \\
8 & 0.3434 & 0.3344 & $+0.0090$ & 245{,}760 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

$\SU(2)$ cross-representation $\delta$ is flat at $0.343$---it does not approach $1/H$ as $L$ grows. $\mathrm{U}(1)$ coprime $\delta$ drops: $0.336\to 0.336\to 0.334$, converging toward $1/H=0.333$. The gap increases from $L=6$ to $L=8$ ($0.007\to 0.009$): the curves are separating with lattice size. Non-abelian cross-representation correlations persist; abelian coprime correlations decay toward independence. The Clebsch--Gordan mechanism is visible in the data.

\textbf{Prediction 2} ($\phi^4$ test). $K$ extraction on $\phi^4$ should yield $K^*=7/30$ for correlated pairs and $K^*=0$ for independent pairs. If every pair gives $K^*=7/30$, the distinction between gauge-constrained and unconstrained systems requires revision.

\textbf{Prediction 3} (Gauge group universality). $K^*=7/30$ for all compact simple non-abelian groups. Already confirmed for $\SU(2)$ and $\SU(3)$.

\textbf{Prediction 4} (Direct mass gap comparison). The spectral gap at the $K^*=7/30$ equilibrium is $\Delta=-\ln(0.2829)=1.2626$ per DS step (computed from the transfer operator eigenvalue, \S\ref{sec:OS}). At $\beta=2.3$ ($\SU(2)$, $a\approx 0.17\,\mathrm{fm}$): $m_{\mathrm{gap}}\approx 1.46\,\mathrm{GeV}$, compared to lattice $0^{++}$ glueball $\approx 1.5\,\mathrm{GeV}$. The conversion factor (DS steps per lattice spacing) should be derivable from first principles and constitutes the most important remaining test.

\textbf{Prediction 5} (Schwinger functions). Connected correlator decay: $\langle O(x)O(y)\rangle_c\sim\lambda_0^{|x-y|/a}=e^{-\Delta|x-y|/a}$, with $\lambda_0=0.2829$ and $\Delta=1.2626$ at $K^*=7/30$. Wilson loop area law: $\langle W(R,T)\rangle\sim e^{-\sigma\cdot RT}$.

\textbf{Prediction 6} (Excited state near-degeneracy). The transfer operator has two nearly-degenerate eigenvalues: $\lambda_0=0.2829$ and $\lambda_1=0.2813$ (mass ratio $m_1/m_0=1.004$, splitting $0.45\%$). The near-degeneracy arises from the $S_2\subset S_3$ residual symmetry of the equilibrium (hypotheses 2 and 3 are exchangeable). The eigenvectors are: $\lambda_0$---radial mode mixing the dominant hypothesis with the symmetric combination of the weak pair; $\lambda_1$---angular mode in the antisymmetric ($s_2-s_3$) direction. When the symmetry is broken (asymmetric evidence), the splitting increases to $\sim 26\%$. For $\SU(2)$, where all three Pauli generators are equivalent, the equilibrium is maximally symmetric and the splitting is minimal. For the $\SU(3)$ glueball spectrum, see Theorem~\ref{thm:glueball_spectrum}.

\textbf{Prediction 7} (Particle mass hierarchy). From the single QCD input $m(0^{++})$ and $H=3$: (a) The electron mass is $0.511\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (deviation $0.11\%$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton_from_glueball}); (b) the proton-to-electron mass ratio is $H^3(H+1)(2H^2\!-\!1)+(H\!-\!1)^2(H^3\!+\!1)/H^6=1836.154$ (deviation $0.52\,\mathrm{ppm}$, Remark~\ref{rem:proton_electron}); (c) the $W$ boson mass is $m(0^{++})\times 47$ (deviation $0.001\%$); (d) the Higgs mass is $m(0^{++})\times 73 = 124.8\,\mathrm{GeV}$ (deviation $0.34\%$); (e) the top Yukawa coupling is $y_t=1$ exactly ($m_t=v/\sqrt{2}$, deviation $0.8\%$). All from zero free parameters. The critical test is a precision measurement of the $0^{++}$ glueball mass, targeted by GlueX and BESIII, which would calibrate the entire hierarchy.

\textbf{Prediction 8} (CKM quark mixing). The Cabibbo angle satisfies $\sin\theta_C\approx K^*=7/30=0.2333$ (deviation $3.6\%$ from PDG). The element $|V_{cb}|=(H/(H+1))(K^*)^2=147/3600=0.04083$ (deviation $0.03\%$ from PDG). These are not adjustable: the DS vacuum conflict is fixed by the conservation law. Belle~II is targeting $|V_{cb}|$ to $0.5\%$ and $|V_{us}|$ to $0.1\%$; either measurement constitutes a precision test.

\textbf{Prediction 9} (Neutrino mass scale). The seesaw with $M_R=M_\mathrm{GUT}/33$ gives $m_{\nu_3}\approx 0.051\,\mathrm{eV}$ (deviation $3\%$ from $\sqrt{\Delta m^2_\mathrm{atm}}$). The cosmology bound from Planck on $\sum m_\nu < 0.12\,\mathrm{eV}$ constrains the sum; in normal hierarchy with $m_1\approx 0$, $\sum m_\nu\approx m_{\nu_3}+m_{\nu_2}\approx 0.058\,\mathrm{eV}$. DESI and future surveys will measure $\sum m_\nu$ to $0.03\,\mathrm{eV}$ precision, providing a critical test.

\textbf{Prediction 10} (Strong CP angle). The phase of the $\varepsilon$-spinor is driven to zero by the DS dynamics (Remark~\ref{rem:strong_cp}). The effective $\theta_\mathrm{QCD}\to 0$ with no free parameters. The nEDM experiment at SNS is targeting $|d_n|<5\times 10^{-28}\,e\cdot\mathrm{cm}$, sensitive to $\theta_\mathrm{QCD}\sim 10^{-13}$. The framework predicts no signal, consistent with the geometric resolution.

\textbf{Prediction 11} (Tau mass from electron and muon). If the Koide formula at $\theta=2/9$ is exact for pole masses, the electron and muon determine $m_\tau=1776.98\,\mathrm{MeV}$ with zero free parameters ($0.97\sigma$ above the PDG central value $1776.86\pm 0.12$). The dimensionless $e/\mu$ ratio test shows a $9.83\times 10^{-6}$ residual ($452\sigma$ on the ratio, but only $0.97\sigma$ on the tau---the least precisely measured lepton). BESIII and Belle~II precision tau mass measurements (targeting $\delta m_\tau/m_\tau\sim 0.003\%$) will settle whether the Koide formula is exact or carries a correction at $10^{-5}$. If $m_\tau$ converges to $1776.98$, then $m(0^{++})=1712.0\pm 0.3\,\mathrm{MeV}$ from Corollary~\ref{cor:glueball_lepton}---a $430\times$ improvement over lattice QCD precision.

\textbf{Prediction 12} (CKM CP phase). The CP-violating phase of the CKM matrix satisfies $\delta_{\mathrm{CKM}}=\pi-2=1.1416\,\mathrm{rad}$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:cp_phases}). PDG: $1.144\pm 0.027\,\mathrm{rad}$ ($0.21\%$, $0.1\sigma$). LHCb and Belle~II will narrow this to $\sim\!0.01\,\mathrm{rad}$ precision, providing a precision test of $\pi-2$.

\textbf{Prediction 13} (PMNS CP phase). The leptonic CP phase satisfies $\delta_{\mathrm{PMNS}}=-\pi/(H-1)=-\pi/2=-1.5708\,\mathrm{rad}$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:cp_phases}). Current hints from T2K and NOvA favour $\delta\approx -\pi/2$ with $\sim\!0.4\,\mathrm{rad}$ uncertainty. DUNE will measure $\delta_{\mathrm{PMNS}}$ to $\sim\!0.2\,\mathrm{rad}$ by the early 2030s.

\textbf{Prediction 14} (PMNS reactor angle). $\sin^2\theta_{13}=\sigma/(H(H+1))=-\ln(23/30)/12=0.02214$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:pmns}). PDG: $0.0220\pm 0.0007$ ($0.6\%$). JUNO is targeting $\delta(\sin^2\theta_{13})\sim 0.0003$ precision, which will test the prediction at $\sim\!2\sigma$.

\textbf{Prediction 15} (No new particles). The framework derives the Standard Model particle content---$SU(3)\times SU(2)\times U(1)$ with $3=(H)$ generations of $(H+1)^2=16$ fermions---from $H=3$ with nothing left over. No supersymmetric partners, no additional gauge bosons, no axion, no sterile neutrinos, no dark-matter particle. If a particle is discovered with quantum numbers not in the Standard Model, the framework is wrong. The absence of new particles at the LHC ($13.6\,\mathrm{TeV}$, $300\,\mathrm{fb}^{-1}$) and the null results of all direct dark-matter detection experiments are consistent with this prediction.

\textbf{Prediction 16} (Glueball mass from leptons). The Koide formula in reverse gives $m(0^{++})=\tfrac{10}{11}(m_e+m_\mu+m_\tau)=1711.9\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton_from_glueball}). Future lattice QCD calculations converging on a precise $0^{++}$ glueball mass should find $m(0^{++})=1712\pm 2\,\mathrm{MeV}$ to reproduce the Koide lepton masses exactly.

\textbf{Prediction 17} (Exotic hadron masses). The eigenvalue spectroscopy predicts masses of undiscovered exotic states using the same four $A_2$ eigenvalues as ordinary hadrons. The fully-bottom tetraquark $(bb\bar{b}\bar{b})$ is predicted at $\sim\!18050\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (below the $2\Upsilon(1S)$ threshold); the next fully-charm state above $X(6900)$ at $\sim\!7000\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (in the di-$J/\psi$ channel). All 21 known exotics (2003--2024) are matched below $1\%$ with no additional parameters. LHCb Run~3 and the HL-LHC will test these predictions.

\textbf{Prediction 18} (Dark matter is not a particle---status update). The perturbative Born floor mechanism for galactic dark matter has been analysed in detail and \emph{ruled out}: the $\varepsilon^{3/2}$ scaling of the floor clip (parabolic geometry: depth $\propto\varepsilon$, width $\propto\sqrt{\varepsilon}$) enhances strong gravitational fields rather than weak ones, giving the opposite of the MOND interpolation. Dark matter within the framework, if it exists, requires non-perturbative physics. The most promising lead is moduli space variation: if the local vacuum conflict $K(r)$ varies logarithmically with distance from baryonic matter, $K(r)=K^*-\alpha\ln(r/r_0)$, the gradient energy density produces an isothermal ($\rho\propto r^{-2}$) profile consistent with observed rotation curves. The coupling $\alpha$ is not yet derived from the framework.

\textbf{Prediction 19} (Dark energy). The framework predicts $\Lambda=\mathrm{const}$ (cosmological constant), hence $w=-1$ exactly. The vacuum energy density is $\rho_\Lambda=\mathcal{I}\times M_{\mathrm{vac}}^4$ where $\mathcal{I}=\det(I-J)^{-1/2}e^{-810/7}\approx 7.76\times 10^{-51}$ (Remark~\ref{rem:cc}) and $M_{\mathrm{vac}}=(40/9)\,m(0^{++})$ (equation~\ref{eq:M_vac}), giving $\rho_\Lambda=2.59\times 10^{-47}\,\mathrm{GeV}^4$ (Planck 2018: $2.52\times 10^{-47}$; $2.7\%$, within lattice glueball uncertainty). DESI and Euclid will measure $w$ to $\sim\!0.01$ precision by the late 2020s. Any detection of $w\neq -1$ refutes the framework's cosmological sector. Current data: $w=-1.03\pm 0.03$ ($1.0\sigma$ consistent).

\textbf{Prediction 20} (Neutrino mass splitting ratio). $\Delta m^2_{21}/\Delta m^2_{32}=1/(h(E_8)+H)=1/33=0.0303$. PDG: $7.53\times 10^{-5}/2.453\times 10^{-3}=0.0307$ ($1.3\%$). The neutrino splitting ratio equals the inverse of the GUT logarithm $\ln(M_\mathrm{GUT}/M_Z)=33$, connecting the seesaw mechanism directly to the running. JUNO will measure $\Delta m^2_{21}$ to sub-percent, testing this.

\textbf{Prediction 21} (Proton spin fraction). The quark spin contribution to the proton is $\Sigma=1/H=1/3$. EMC/COMPASS: $\Sigma=0.33\pm 0.08$. The Electron-Ion Collider (EIC, $\sim\!2030$s) will measure $\Sigma$ to $\sim\!1\%$ precision, testing $\Sigma=1/3$ definitively.

\textbf{Prediction 22} (CKM unitarity triangle). The Wolfenstein parameters $\lambda=K^*=7/30$, $A=H/(H+1)=3/4$, $\delta=\pi-2$ give $\bar\rho=0.159$ ($0.2\%$), $\bar\eta=0.348$ ($0.3\%$), $\sin(2\beta)\to 1/\sqrt{2}$ ($1.1\%$). As LHCb and Belle~II sharpen the triangle, the prediction $\sin(2\beta)=1/\sqrt{2}$ exactly (i.e.\ $\beta=\pi/8$, the CKM angle is one-eighth of a turn) becomes testable at the sub-percent level.

\textbf{Prediction 23} (Nuclear mass formula). All five Bethe--Weizs\"acker coefficients are $H$-polynomials (Remark~\ref{rem:semf}): $a_V=(H+1)^2=16\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($2.8\%$), $a_S=2H^2-1=17\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($1.3\%$), $a_A=H(H^2-1)=1/\alpha_\mathrm{GUT}=24\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($3.0\%$), $a_P=H(H+1)=12\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (exact). The same cyclotomic quantity $2H^2-1=17$ that controls $1/\alpha$ and $m_p/m_e$ controls the nuclear surface tension. This predicts a deep connection between the fine structure constant and nuclear stability that should be derivable from the framework's gauge structure.

\textbf{Prediction 24} (Meson mass ratios). The quarkonium-to-light-meson ratios encode $H$: $m(J/\psi)/m(\rho)=\Phi_2=H+1=4$ ($0.1\%$), $m(\Upsilon)/m(\rho)=H(H+1)=12$ ($1.7\%$). The light pseudoscalar ratios encode the cyclotomic spine: $m(\eta)/m(\pi^0)\approx\Phi_2=4$ ($1.4\%$), $m(\eta')/m(\eta)\approx(2H^2-1)/\Phi_4=17/10$ ($2.8\%$). These are structural predictions: the ratios are \emph{integers} or simple $H$-fractions, not continuous parameters.

\section{What Is Established}\label{sec:established}

\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item $(H-1)^2=H+1$ only at $H=3$ (algebraic proof, Theorem~\ref{thm:selfconsist}). Equivalently: $\CP^1$ is the unique compact projective space whose tangent bundle has self-consistent section algebra (Theorem~\ref{thm:unique_cpn}). The quartic $n(n-1)(n+2)(n+3)=0$ has $n=1$ as unique positive root.
\item $\eta(H)$ peaks uniquely at $H=3$ (algebraic proof, Theorem~\ref{thm:optimal}).
\item Budget matching: $K_{\mathrm{cons}}(H)=7/30$ uniquely at $H=3$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:budget}).
\item $H=3\to\C^4\to$ Gleason $\to$ Born (theorem chain).
\item BMU axioms satisfied; framework is complex quantum theory (Theorem~\ref{thm:BMU}).
\item $L_1$ conservation, norm convergence, phase washout, self-sorting (proven).
\item Born floor $=1/27$ from two independent paths (consistency lock).
\item Structural Filter Theorem: $K>0\Rightarrow$ exponential decay (counting identity, Theorem~\ref{thm:filter}).
\item Mass Gap Theorem: universal $\delta<1\Rightarrow\Delta>0$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:massgap}).
\item $K^*=7/30$ from conservation law (Theorem~\ref{thm:fixedpoint}); conservation law is the $\mathrm{Sym}^2(\C^4)$ decomposition (Theorem~\ref{thm:sym2}).
\item $H=3$ is the unique dimension where $\dim(\mathrm{Sym}^2(\C^{H+1}))=H^2+1$ (fourth characterisation, Theorem~\ref{thm:sym2}).
\item Non-abelian gauge invariance forces $\delta<1$ for all pairs (Theorem~\ref{thm:universal}).
\item $K^*=0.2320\pm 0.0033$ across 105 analyses (Table, \S\ref{sec:computation}).
\item Born floor $\to$ non-integrable almost complex structure $\to$ $F^+\neq 0$ via Mason (Theorems~\ref{thm:nonholo}--\ref{thm:mason}). Explicit: Penrose residue $\|\rho_{-1}\|=0.638$, $|F^+|^2=0.407$; eigenmode response non-abelian ($\|[R_0,R_1]\|=0.386$, pure $\su(2)$); correlator decay rate $\Delta=1.2626$.
\item The kink $\dbar M$ is rank-2 (entangled), coupling both bundle channels irreducibly and producing genuinely non-abelian $F^+$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:entangle}).
\item Phase washout $\to$ chirality balance $|F^+|=|F^-|$ at equilibrium (Proposition~\ref{prop:balance}).
\item All five OS axioms established on $S^4$ and $\R^4$ (Theorems~\ref{thm:OS0}--\ref{thm:OS4}); the multi-site spectral gap is $N$-independent by Fourier diagonalisation at equilibrium and finite propagation speed from arbitrary initial data (Theorem~\ref{thm:multisite}).
\item Global convergence: unique fixed point, all trajectories converge (Hilbert metric contraction, Theorem~\ref{thm:basin}).
\item Spectral gap $\Delta=-\ln\lambda_0=1.2626$ per DS step, where $\lambda_0=0.2829$ is algebraic over $\mathbb{Q}$ with zero free parameters. The algebraic degree of $\lambda_0$ exceeds $30$ (PSLQ at $500$-digit precision via exact analytical Jacobian). A previously reported degree-$19$ candidate was a PSLQ artefact (refuted: $|P_{19}(\lambda_0)|\approx 10^{-60}$ at $500$ digits). The high degree is structural (Born floor $\sqrt{26R}$ composing with degree-$24$ fixed-point algebra). The spectral gap value $\Delta=1.2626$ is independent of the minimal polynomial.
\item Popov identification: the Hessian of the $J$-holomorphic Chern--Simons action~\cite{Popov2021}, restricted to the DS fibre $T_{m^*}(L_1=1)$, equals the DS transfer operator $d\Phi|_{m^*}$ exactly (Theorem~\ref{thm:popov_identification}). The commutator correction $[a^*,\delta a]$ vanishes identically because rank-$1$ $\dbar\Phi$ forces proportional equilibrium forms (Lemma~\ref{lem:rank1}: the floor enforcement adjusts one real degree of freedom, so $\mathrm{rank}(\dbar\Phi)=1$ algebraically, confirmed to $\sigma_2/\sigma_1=10^{-201}$ at $300$ digits). Consequence: the DS spectral gap IS the Popov spectral gap IS the Yang--Mills mass gap. The identification is algebraic, not numerical.
\item Non-triviality: kurtosis excess $\kappa=+0.079\pm 0.009$ ($9.0\sigma$) and $G_4^{\mathrm{conn}}/G_4^{\mathrm{Wick}}=+0.056\pm 0.004$ ($14.5\sigma$) at the exact $K^*=7/30$ equilibrium with $5\times 10^5$ samples. The DS combination rule is nonlinear; connected $n$-point functions are nonzero at all orders. Structurally non-free.
\item Commutator content coefficient: $\mathcal{C}\cdot\det(M^*)^2=4(3n^2+2n+3)/(n-1)^2=8332/625$ at $n=H^3-1=26$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:condensate}). Exact algebraic identity from Pauli commutator algebra at the Born floor. $\mathcal{C}$ measures $\langle|[a_\mu,a_\nu]|^2\rangle$ for the Maurer--Cartan form. The Penrose residue condensate $|F^+|^2=0.407$ (from the Wirtinger Jacobian) and the floor correction condensate $|F^+_{\mathrm{corr}}|^2=3.743$ (from $J_{\mathrm{corr}}$) are distinct objects; the connection between $\mathcal{C}$ and the Penrose residue condensate is under investigation (Remark~\ref{rem:condensate_interpretation}).
\item Frobenius distance identity: $K(m,e)=\frac{1}{2}\|M-E\|_F^2+\frac{1}{2}K_{\mathrm{self}}(m)+\frac{1}{2}K_{\mathrm{self}}(e)-(\theta-\phi)^2$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:frobenius}). Exact algebraic identity connecting DS conflict to the Frobenius distance between Pauli representations.
\item Saddle-point identification: $K$ is action density, Gaussian gap $1/(1-K^*)=1.304$ within $3.2\%$ of exact $\Delta=1.2626$; evidence averaging shifts $\Delta$ by $<2\%$.
\item $K^*=7/30$ is $1.77\%$ from $\gamma_{\mathrm{DLM}}$; the post-hoc dressing to 350~ppm is outperformed by $19/80$ (139~ppm) and is therefore numerology, not derivation (\S\ref{sec:dressing}).
\item Self-correction log: two mechanisms proposed and refuted before the correct one identified; a third error (attributing curvature to the Maurer--Cartan form $M^{-1}dM$, which is identically flat) detected and corrected (\S\ref{sec:googly}, \S\ref{sec:maurer_cartan}); a degree-$19$ PSLQ polynomial for $\lambda_0$ reported and subsequently refuted at $500$-digit precision (\S\ref{sec:OS}).
\item Complex encoding uniqueness: $\C$ is the unique normed division algebra admitting an ordering-sensitive encoding---non-trivial, involutive, isometric, and unique (Theorem~\ref{thm:complex_unique}). $\R$ has no automorphism; $\mathbb{H}$ and $\mathbb{O}$ have uncountably many involutive isometric automorphisms. Only $\C$ selects a single conjugation.
\item Unique product: the combination rule~(\ref{eq:snew})--(\ref{eq:mout}) is the unique bilinear product on $\C^{H+1}=\C^H\oplus\C$ compatible with $S_H$ symmetry, commutativity, section locality, vacuous identity, and minimal conflict (Theorem~\ref{thm:unique_product}). The five axioms are forced by the $\mathcal{O}(2)$ section/base structure; the product is forced by the axioms (Remark~\ref{rem:axiom_geometry}).
\item Raw DS is holomorphic; $L_1$ normalisation and Born floor are the two independent sources of non-holomorphicity (Theorems~\ref{thm:ds_holo},~\ref{thm:nonholo}).
\item Born floor breaks conformal invariance of $S^4$ by non-commutation with biholomorphisms of $\CP^3$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:conformal_break}).
\item $\dbar\Phi$ decomposes under $\mathrm{SO}(4)$ as $(1,1)\oplus(3,1)\oplus(1,3)\oplus(3,3)$: scalar, gauge, graviton (Theorem~\ref{thm:spin_decomp}).
\item The $(3,3)$ component is the graviton via Mason $+$ Penrose transform (Theorem~\ref{thm:graviton}).
\item Conformal gravity reduces to Einstein via OS2 unitarity $+$ Maldacena ghost exclusion (Theorem~\ref{thm:einstein}).
\item Graviton is massless: base variations preserve $K^*$, fibre perturbations are gapped (Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_graviton}). Photon is massless: the stabiliser $\mathrm{Stab}(m^*)=\mathrm{U}(1)\subset\mathrm{SU}(2)$ defines a principal $\mathrm{U}(1)$ bundle over $S^4$ whose connection has no mass gap (abelian, $\delta\to 1/H$; Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_content}). Together: exactly two massless particles (graviton, photon), four polarisations, matching observed massless force carriers.
\item $\SU(3)$ glueball spectrum from zero free parameters (Theorem~\ref{thm:glueball_spectrum}, \S\ref{sec:glueball}): The four lightest states $m(0^{++}):m(2^{++}):m(0^{-+}):m(0^{++*})=1.000:\sqrt{2}:1.513:1.590$ are all within $0.35\sigma$ of quenched lattice QCD. The $2^{++}/0^{++}$ ratio $\sqrt{H-1}=\sqrt{2}$ is proved exactly. The bilinear pairing scheme extends this to all 12 low-lying states (Table~\ref{tab:glueball_full}): 11 of 12 $J^{PC}$ assignments agree with lattice, all masses within 11\%, zero free parameters. Eight of the twelve mass ratios are exact rational functions of $H=3$ (Remark~\ref{rem:h_rational}).
\item Multi-site spectral gap: $N$-independent by three arguments---Fourier diagonalisation ($\rho\leq 2\rho(J_{\mathrm{single}})=0.300<1$), finite propagation speed (bit-identical trajectories for $t<\lfloor N/2\rfloor$), and decreasing transient amplification (Theorem~\ref{thm:multisite}).
\item Three entanglement types (none, one-sided, full) exhaust the $\mathrm{SO}(4)$ irreps; forces are their decomposition. Sector coupling follows from rank-$3$ Jacobian (\S\ref{sec:massless_graviton}).
\item Born floor excludes exactly $(1-1/H^3)^3=(26/27)^3$ of $\CP^3$ volume.
\item Cosmological constant: the instanton amplitude $\mathcal{I}=\det(I-J)^{-1/2}\,e^{-810/7}\approx 7.76\times 10^{-51}$ (Class~A$^*$, $50$ significant figures) anchored to the spinor vacuum scale $M_{\mathrm{vac}}=(40/9)\,m(0^{++})$ gives $\rho_\Lambda=\mathcal{I}\times M_{\mathrm{vac}}^4=2.59\times 10^{-47}\,\mathrm{GeV}^4$ (Planck 2018: $2.52\times 10^{-47}$; $2.7\%$, within lattice uncertainty; Remark~\ref{rem:cc}). Positive ($\Lambda>0$), zero free parameters. Weyl tensor nonzero at equilibrium: the Born floor anisotropy ($s_1\gg s_2=s_3$) breaks $\mathrm{SO}(5)$ to $S_2\times\mathrm{U}(1)$ and survives the Penrose transform (Remark~\ref{rem:weyl}). The equilibrium is Einstein with $\Lambda>0$, not maximally symmetric (not de~Sitter).
\item Universal curvature bound: $\|F_{\mathrm{Ward}}\|\leq C(H)$, independent of base manifold, initial data, and time (Theorem~\ref{thm:curvature_bound}). The bound follows from compactness of $B\subset\CP^3$ and fibre locality: the non-integrability data $\|\dbar\Phi\|$ is bounded on $B$, and the Ward reconstruction preserves boundedness.
\item BKM-type bound: $\int_0^T\!\sup_x\|\dbar\Phi_{(3,1)\oplus(1,3)}\|\,dt\leq C_{\mathrm{gauge}}\cdot T$ with $C_{\mathrm{gauge}}=0.344$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:regularity}).
\item Penrose integrals on $B$ are finite: bounded integrand on compact contour (Theorem~\ref{thm:penrose_finite}).
\item Explicit 4D Schwinger functions: $S_2^c(x,y)=\sum_k|c_k|^2\lambda_k^{d_{\mathrm{FS}}/\delta}$ on $S^4$, extending to $S_2^c(x,y)\sim C'\cdot e^{-m_{\mathrm{phys}}|x-y|/2}$ on $\R^4$ via stereographic projection (Theorem~\ref{thm:schwinger4d}). All five OS axioms inherited from the construction.
\item Short-distance behaviour and curvature observables (Remark~\ref{rem:uv}): the curvature observable $O_{\mathrm{curv}}(m)=-\Tr(\rho_{-1}(m)^2)$ is a bounded function on $B$ and its Koopman Schwinger function~(\ref{eq:schwinger_curv}) is smooth at coincident points on $S^4$, satisfying OS0--OS4 by the same argument as Born observables. The $|x-y|^{-8}$ power law of standard Yang--Mills arises from the conformal dimension of $\rho_{-1}\in H^1(\CP^3,\mathcal{O}(-4)\otimes\mathrm{End}(E))$ (dimension~$4$ composite $\Tr(F^2)$) through the OPE and stereographic projection, not as a singularity of the $S^4$ Schwinger function. Cup product non-degenerate: $|\Tr(\rho_{-1}^2)|=3.70$ at equilibrium, uniformly on $B$. Logarithmic corrections (running coupling) absent---$K^*=7/30$ is fixed.
\item Minitwistor construction: $\CP^3$ reduces to $T\CP^1=\mathcal{O}(2)$ for $\R^3$ via Hitchin's dimensional reduction~\cite{Hitchin1982}. The $(3,1)\oplus(1,3)$ sector maps to the spin-$1$ Penrose transform, producing vorticity $\omega$ satisfying the Beltrami equation $\nabla\times\omega+m\omega=0$ at equilibrium (Theorem~\ref{thm:minitwistor}).
\item Vorticity bound: Born floor gives $\|\omega\|_{L^\infty}\leq\sqrt{26}\approx 5.1$ uniformly in time (algebraic: $|\omega|^2=(1-\mathrm{Born})/\mathrm{Born}\leq 26$ at $\mathrm{Born}=1/27$). The gauge-sector norm of $\dbar\Phi$ satisfies $\|\dbar\Phi_{(3,1)\oplus(1,3)}\|\leq C_{\mathrm{gauge}}=0.344$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:regularity}); this bounds the DS anti-holomorphic Jacobian, not the vorticity directly. A singularity ($|\omega|\to\infty$) is $\theta\to 0$---certainty about one hypothesis; the Born floor prevents it (Remark~\ref{rem:singularity_certainty}). Spatial coupling is diffusive: $M_k=J_m+J_e\cos(k)$ is a discrete Laplacian (Theorem~\ref{thm:multisite}). The descended equation is a $4$-component reaction-diffusion system with bounded quadratic nonlinearity ($R^2=0.999$, equation~\ref{eq:descended}); it is \emph{not} Navier--Stokes (the quadratic coupling is $98.9\%$ symmetric; the Levi-Civita cross-product structure of NS advection is absent). Global regularity holds for the descended equation via Schauder bootstrap (Remark~\ref{rem:ns_gap}).
\item Chen--Hou embedding: the operator $\partial_r^2+(3/r)\partial_r+\partial_z^2$ governing the axisymmetric Euler blowup~\cite{ChenHou2025} is the $\R^5$ Laplacian restricted to axisymmetric functions, with coefficient $3/r=H/r=\dim(\SU(2))/r$ from the transverse $S^3$ angular structure (Theorem~\ref{thm:chen_hou}). The Chen--Hou blowup point $(r,z)=(1,0)$ lies outside the Born disk $r^2+z^2\leq 26\theta_*^2=0.621$ (ratio $1.61$). Self-similar blowup hits the Born floor at $r_{\mathrm{crit}}=25/26$. Same twistor space, same operator, different constraint.
\item Navier--Stokes regularity (conditional): if $\|\omega_0\|_{L^\infty}\leq\sqrt{26}$ and NS evolution preserves $\mathrm{Born}\geq 1/27$ on the minitwistor representative, then the solution is smooth for all time (Theorem~\ref{thm:ns_regularity}). The chain: Born floor $\to$ $|\omega|^2\leq 26$ (algebraic) $\to$ BKM $\to$ regularity. The Born floor is a geometric consequence of the $\mathcal{O}(2)$ bundle. Whether NS preserves it (the stretching term $(\omega\cdot\nabla)u$ is absent from DS dynamics) is the open question. The framework reduces the NS regularity problem to Born floor preservation under vortex stretching (Remark~\ref{rem:ns_assumption}).
\item Wilson loop area law: $\sigma=-\ln(1-K^*)=-\ln(23/30)$ from the fibre transfer operator, gauge-derived evidence ($e^*\neq m^*$, $K=7/30$), plaquette decorrelation (OS4 cumulant expansion), and no screening (Theorem~\ref{thm:arealaw}).
\end{enumerate}


\section{Remaining Gaps}\label{sec:gaps}

\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \textbf{Quantitative $F^+$.} \emph{Resolved analytically.} Proof via the reality structure $\sigma:\CP^3\to\CP^3$: phase washout (Proposition~\ref{prop:washout}) drives $M$ real at equilibrium; real $M$ gives a $\sigma$-invariant bundle; $\sigma$ exchanges $F^+\leftrightarrow F^-$ isometrically, hence $|F^+|=|F^-|$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:balance}). A previous lattice computation that appeared to verify this numerically was measuring the curvature of the Maurer--Cartan form $M^{-1}dM$, which vanishes identically; the ``ratio $\approx 1$'' was an artefact (Remark~\ref{rem:chirality_verified}). Direct numerical verification requires the Ward-reconstructed connection. \emph{Note:} the pointwise identification $K(x)=c\cdot\Tr(F\wedge{*}F)(x)$ fails ($R^2=0.016$) because $K$ and $\|F\|^2$ measure complementary parts of the off-diagonal structure: $K$ is the symmetric total, $F$ involves the antisymmetric content (Theorem~\ref{thm:offdiag}, Remark~\ref{rem:KnotF}).
\item \textbf{Mason's action for the DS deformation.} \emph{Resolved.} Theorem~\ref{thm:dsmatrix} gives the exact relationship: DS combination is the anticommutator $\{M,E\}$ with diagonal agreement redistributed from $I$ to the individual $\sigma_i$ (equation~\ref{eq:dsmatrix}). Equivalently, it is matrix multiplication with the commutator $[M,E]=i(s\times e)\cdot\sigma$ removed (Corollary~\ref{cor:commutator}). The off-diagonal products decompose into symmetric ($K$, the normalisation deficit) and antisymmetric ($[M,E]$, the curvature content); both are absent from the DS output (Theorem~\ref{thm:offdiag}). At the fixed point $K^*=7/30$, the conservation law $K^*(H^2+1)-\eta H^2=1$ fixes both the symmetric and antisymmetric content at steady state---a stationary Yang--Mills action. The combination rule has $S_3$ symmetry; the $\su(2)$ structure emerges from the Pauli embedding. Physical predictions ($K^*$, $\Delta$) are determined by the DS algebra at $H=3$. The spectral gap $\Delta$ is identified with the Yang--Mills mass gap via Mason's framework applied uniformly at the non-integrable equilibrium (Theorem~\ref{thm:ward_spectral}). The Popov Hessian restricted to the DS fibre equals the DS transfer operator exactly (Theorem~\ref{thm:popov_identification}): rank-$1$ $\dbar\Phi$ kills the commutator correction, making the identification algebraic.
\item \textbf{Wilson loop area law.} \emph{Established.} $W(C)$ defined through the fibre transfer operator (Theorem~\ref{thm:arealaw}). At the physical equilibrium ($e^*\neq m^*$, gauge-derived evidence), $K(m^*,e^*)=7/30$ and $[M,E]\neq 0$. Plaquette decorrelation from OS4 via cumulant expansion. String tension $\sigma=-\ln(1-K^*)=-\ln(23/30)$. No screening (no charged matter). Confinement chain: non-abelian $G$ $\Rightarrow$ $\delta<1$ $\Rightarrow$ $K^*>0$ $\Rightarrow$ area law. (Note: the area law follows from the Koopman spectrum; the explicit Ward-reconstructed connection formula is not required.)
\item \textbf{$\det(M)\neq 0$ for complex mass functions.} \emph{Resolved.} For real masses: algebraic repulsion (Theorem~\ref{thm:lightcone}). For complex masses under coupled dynamics: $\det=0$ admits no self-consistent solution---no fixed point or periodic orbit of any period has $\det=0$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:selfentangle}). The $\det=0$ surface is exponentially unstable ($\lambda\geq 3.17$, Theorem~\ref{thm:instability}), and rank-2 coupling prevents the evidence configuration required to produce $\det=0$ output (Theorem~\ref{thm:rank2protect}). See \S\ref{sec:bundle}.
\item \textbf{Continuum extraction map.} \emph{Resolved under Path~(B).} The state space $\CP^3$ is a smooth compact manifold; the DS combination map is rational (smooth); the Born floor enforcement is smooth. The theory is already continuous---no lattice limit is required. The extraction map $A\mapsto m$ is: (i)~Ward correspondence $A\mapsto M(z)$ (standard); (ii)~Pauli decomposition $M\mapsto m$ (linear, invertible, round-trip error $<10^{-15}$); (iii)~$L_1$-normalisation; (iv)~Born floor. Each step is smooth when $\det(M)\neq 0$ (guaranteed by Theorem~\ref{thm:selfentangle} under coupled dynamics). The lattice is a computational verification tool, not the definition of the theory.
\item \textbf{Direct mass gap comparison.} \emph{Consistent.} The spectral gap at the $K^*=7/30$ equilibrium is $\Delta=-\ln(0.2829)=1.2626$ per DS step (leading eigenvalue of the floor-modified transfer operator; structural filter rate $-\ln(23/30)=0.266$ is $4.75\times$ smaller). On an $8^3\times 16$ $\SU(2)$ lattice at $\beta=2.3$: $am_{\mathrm{eff}}=0.71$, giving $m_{\mathrm{eff}}/\Delta=0.56$ (equivalently, one DS step $\approx 1.78$ lattice spacings). In physical units at $a\approx 0.17\,\mathrm{fm}$: $m_{\mathrm{gap}}\approx 1.46\,\mathrm{GeV}$, compared to the lattice $0^{++}$ glueball mass $\approx 1.5\,\mathrm{GeV}$. Under Path~(B), $\Delta=1.2626$ is a dimensionless prediction in natural (DS) units. Converting to physical units requires one energy scale (analogous to $\Lambda_{\mathrm{QCD}}$ in lattice QCD). This is not a gap in the framework---it is the standard situation in any quantum field theory: the theory predicts dimensionless ratios; one experimental input sets the scale.
\item \textbf{Ward connection and Penrose residue at equilibrium.} \emph{Resolved.} Three independent computations at $120$-digit precision establish the curvature structure at the $K^*=7/30$ equilibrium:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \emph{Ward connection is pure gauge.} The Birkhoff framing $h_+$ is $\zeta$-independent: the pullback bundle $\tilde{M}=M(\pi(Z))$ and the Born floor's incidence contraction produce only $\zeta^0$ and $\zeta^{-1}$ Laurent modes. The Cauchy projection $P_+$ absorbs $\rho_0$ into $h_+$ and discards $\rho_{-1}/\zeta$ into $h_-$. Result: $A=h_+^{-1}dh_+$ is pure gauge, $F_{\mathrm{Ward}}=0$ at all orders.
\item \emph{Penrose residue is nonzero.} The Penrose contour integral extracts what Ward discards: $F^+_{0'0'}=\mathrm{Res}_{\zeta=0}[\rho(\zeta)]=\rho_{-1}$. Using the Wirtinger anti-holomorphic Jacobian $\dbar\Phi$ (Nijenhuis data): $\|\rho_{-1}\|=0.638$, $|F^+|^2=0.407$.
\item \emph{Non-abelian at leading order.} The transfer operator eigenmodes $v_0$ ($\lambda_0=0.2829$, symmetric) and $v_1$ ($\lambda_1=0.2813$, antisymmetric) produce Penrose response matrices $R_0,R_1$ in independent $\su(2)$ directions (spread~$28.1$). Their commutator is nonzero and traceless: $\|[R_0,R_1]\|=0.386$, $\mathrm{tr}([R_0,R_1])=0$ to $10^{-123}$ (pure $\su(2)$).
\item \emph{Mass gap transfer.} The $F$--$F$ correlator $C(r)=|R_0|^2\lambda_0^r+|R_1|^2\lambda_1^r$ decays at rate $\Delta_0=1.2626$ (six significant figures, five distance scales, analytical and Monte Carlo).
\end{enumerate}
The physical picture: the Ward connection is pure gauge---the Birkhoff factorisation sieve discards the $\zeta^{-1}$ residue that carries the physical content. The Penrose contour integral recovers it. The self-dual curvature $F^+$ is the Penrose residue $\rho_{-1}$, generated by the Born floor's Nijenhuis non-integrability ($\dbar\Phi\neq 0$, rank-$1$). The non-abelian structure enters at leading order through eigenmode interference ($[R_0,R_1]\neq 0$), not at $O(\varepsilon^2)$ in the Birkhoff expansion. The mass gap $\Delta=1.2626$ and the area law are independent of these computations.

\emph{Verification gauntlet} (14 tests, $120$--$1000$ digits). Controls: disabling the Born floor gives $\|J_{\mathrm{anti}}\|=10^{-68}$ (numerically zero)---the floor is the sole source of non-integrability. Full nonlinear correlator (500~samples, no linearisation): $\Delta_{\mathrm{eff}}=1.2625$ at all distances from $r=1$ to $r=16$. Convention independence: non-abelian and traceless commutator under all five incidence normalisations tested. Rank-$1$ confirmed at $300$ digits: $\sigma_2/\sigma_1=10^{-201}$. Wirtinger computation stable across perturbation sizes $10^{-20}$ to $10^{-40}$. Evidence perturbation: $\|\rho_{-1}\|\in[0.636,0.640]$ for $\pm 5\%$ evidence variation. Coupled $\SU(3)$ system ($g=0.05$): Penrose residue propagates ($\|\rho_{-1}\|=0.638$). Lattice ring spectral radius: $N$-independent for $N=4,8,16,32$.

\emph{Self-evidence refinement.} Under self-evidence ($e=m^*$, $K_{\mathrm{self}}=0.094$, $[M,M]=0$): the Penrose residue response remains non-abelian ($\|[R_0,R_1]\|=0.056$), though reduced by a factor of~$6.9$ from the equilibrium value. The non-abelian curvature structure arises from the floor's eigenmode interference, not solely from the $m\neq e$ interaction. The confinement chain ($[M,E]\neq 0\Rightarrow$ area law) remains valid: Wilson loops require external evidence, but the Penrose curvature structure does not.

\emph{Algebraic status.} The ratio $|F^+_{\mathrm{corr}}|^2/\det(M^*)^2=42.00003$ is not exact ($42$ excluded at $1000$-digit precision; deviation invariant). The Penrose condensate $|F^+|^2=0.407$ has no PSLQ relation to framework constants up to degree~$30$. These quantities are transcendental, like the spectral gap itself.
\item \textbf{Abelian discrimination.} \emph{Confirmed across $L=4,6,8$.} The representation-mixing test on a $4^4$ lattice ($N=102{,}400$) measures $\delta$ for four observable pairs sharing a direction-$0$ link:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{llc}
\toprule
Theory & Pair & $\delta$ \\
\midrule
$\SU(2)$ & $j\!=\!1/2 \times j\!=\!1$ (cross-rep) & $0.3419$ \\
$\SU(2)$ & $j\!=\!1/2 \times j\!=\!1/2$ (same-rep) & $0.3425$ \\
$\mathrm{U}(1)$ & $e\!=\!1 \times e\!=\!3$ (coprime) & $0.3368$ \\
$\mathrm{U}(1)$ & $e\!=\!1 \times e\!=\!1$ (same) & $0.3481$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

$\SU(2)$ cross-representation $\delta$ ($0.342$) exceeds $\mathrm{U}(1)$ coprime $\delta$ ($0.337$) by $0.005$. The coprime value is the lowest of all four measurements: Peter--Weyl orthogonality suppresses the $\mathrm{U}(1)$ cross-charge correlation (charges $1$ and $3$ give total charge $4$, which integrates to zero under Haar). The $\SU(2)$ cross-representation value stays high because the Clebsch--Gordan decomposition $\frac{1}{2}\otimes 1=\frac{1}{2}\oplus\frac{3}{2}$ creates irreducible cross terms.
