Combining: $\lambda_{S_-}=\delta s_{2,\mathrm{final}}/\varepsilon=\alpha\cdot(e_2^*+\phi^*)/(1-K^*)$, which is~(\ref{eq:colour_diff}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[$A_2$ sector decomposition]\label{rem:A2_sectors}
The $8\times 8$ coupled $A_2$ Jacobian decomposes under the $\Z_2$ node-swap symmetry into two $4\times 4$ blocks: the symmetric sector $V_+$ (nodes in phase) and the antisymmetric sector $V_-$ (nodes out of phase). Each block inherits the $s_2\leftrightarrow s_3$ decomposition into a $3\times 3$ radial block and a $1\times 1$ angular block (Proposition~\ref{prop:colour_diff}).

The four physical eigenvalues split:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\hline
Sector & Eigenvalues & Physical content \\
\hline
Antisymmetric ($V_-$) & $\lambda_0=0.5022$, $\lambda_1=0.4745$ & coloured ($\mathbf{3}\oplus\bar{\mathbf{3}}$) \\
Symmetric ($V_+$) & $\lambda_2=0.3527$, $\lambda_3=0.3344$ & colour-singlet \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The spectral radius lies in $V_-$, not $V_+$. This is specific to $A_2$: the $\Z_2$ orbit exhausts the diagram (no fixed node), so the junction-node cancellation argument of Theorem~\ref{thm:folding_invariance} does not apply. Antisymmetric perturbations (nodes out of phase) enhance the evidence coupling---if $\delta m_2=-\delta m_1$, the evidence for node~$1$ is $e^*-g(\delta m_2-0)=e^*+g\,\delta m_1$, a constructive feedback---producing larger eigenvalues than the symmetric sector.

The single-site Jacobian has two significant eigenvalues: $\lambda_{\mathrm{rad}}=0.2829$ (radial, from the $3\times 3$ block) and $\lambda_{S_-}=0.2813$ (angular, from Proposition~\ref{prop:colour_diff}). Under $A_2$ coupling, each splits into an enhanced antisymmetric mode and a suppressed symmetric mode, producing the four coupled eigenvalues. The splitting magnitude is controlled by $K^*=7/30$: stronger equilibrium conflict produces wider splitting.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Eigenvalue mode classification]\label{cor:mode_classification}
The four nontrivial $A_2$ Jacobian eigenvalues split into two radial (floor-active, curvature-sourcing) modes and two angular (holomorphic, floor-invisible) modes. Combined with the node symmetry (Lie theory) and light-point spin assignment (Theorem~\ref{thm:lightpoint_decomp}), every eigenvalue carries a unique set of spatial quantum numbers:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{clcccl}
\hline
Mode & Subspace & Spin & Colour & Floor & Identity \\
\hline
$e_0$ ($\lambda_0=0.5022$) & radial ($\delta s_1$) & $\sim\!0$ & $\mathbf{3}\oplus\bar{\mathbf{3}}$ & active & gluon \\
$e_1$ ($\lambda_1=0.4745$) & angular ($s_2\!-\!s_3$) & $\tfrac{1}{2}$ & $\mathbf{3}\oplus\bar{\mathbf{3}}$ & off & quark (Thm~\ref{thm:quark_mode}) \\
$e_2$ ($\lambda_2=0.3527$) & angular ($s_2\!-\!s_3$) & $\tfrac{1}{2}$ & singlet & off & lepton direction \\
$e_3$ ($\lambda_3=0.3344$) & radial ($\delta s_1$) & $\sim\!0$ & singlet & active & gluon \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The classification follows from: (i)~$S_2$ symmetry at equilibrium forces exact radial/angular eigenvector separation (simultaneous diagonalisation of $D\Phi$ and the swap $s_2\leftrightarrow s_3$); (ii)~angular modes satisfy $\delta S=\delta S_q=0$, so the Born floor does not fire (Proposition~\ref{prop:quark_floor}); (iii)~radial modes have $\delta S\neq 0$, $\delta S_q\neq 0$, triggering the enslaving mechanism (Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}) and sourcing curvature $F^+$ through $\dbar\Phi\neq 0$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:nonholo}). Only the floor-active (radial) modes generate the gauge field; the floor-invisible (angular) modes are fermion directions that propagate without generating curvature at linear order.
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[Massless particle classification]\label{rem:massless_classification}
The framework contains exactly three types of massless excitation:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item \emph{Graviton} (spin~$2$): smooth variation of the equilibrium orientation $\mathbf{n}:S^4\to S^2$ across the base manifold. The transfer operator returns $\lambda=1$ exactly (Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_graviton}). This is a base-direction mode.
\item \emph{Photon} (spin~$1$): the unbroken gauge connection $\mathrm{Stab}(m^*)=\mathrm{U}(1)\subset\SU(2)$, which rotates the $s_2$--$s_3$ plane while preserving the dominant direction $s_1$. Because $\mathrm{U}(1)$ is abelian, $K^*=0$ for the photon sector (Remark~\ref{rem:chirality}): the floor never fires, so no mass gap is generated. The photon is a fibre-direction gauge connection, not a Jacobian eigenvalue.
\item \emph{Gluons} (spin~$1$, $\times 8$): the non-abelian gauge curvature $F^+$ generated by the Born floor acting on radial modes. Perturbatively massless (gauge invariance), but confining: physical colour-singlet states (glueballs) carry mass gap $\Delta_0$.
\end{enumerate}
Everything else---$W^\pm$, $Z^0$, all fermions, the Higgs---couples to the Born floor and acquires mass. The photon and graviton are the unique modes orthogonal to the mass-generating mechanism: the photon is orthogonal in the fibre (abelian stabiliser), the graviton in the base (orientation zero-mode).
\end{remark}

\subsection{Gauge group and electroweak structure}\label{sec:gauge_structure}

\begin{theorem}[$\SU(3)\times\SU(2)\times\mathrm{U}(1)$ product structure]\label{thm:gauge_product}
The physical symmetry group of the framework at $H=3$ is $\SU(3)\times\SU(2)\times\mathrm{U}(1)$, with the three factors acting on independent tensor indices and commuting trivially. The total generator count is $H^2-1+H+1=H(H+1)=12$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{$\SU(3)$}: the DS combination rule~(\ref{eq:snew})--(\ref{eq:mout}) satisfies $s_{\mathrm{new},\sigma(i)}=s_{\sigma(i)}e_{\sigma(i)}+s_{\sigma(i)}\phi+\theta e_{\sigma(i)}$ for every permutation $\sigma\in S_3$, giving a discrete $S_3$ symmetry of the dynamics. The unique simple compact Lie algebra with Weyl group $S_3\cong\mathrm{Dih}_3$ is $A_2=\mathfrak{su}(3)$ (Bourbaki~\cite{Bourbaki}). The $\SU(3)$ acts on the Dynkin node labels (colour index).

\emph{$\SU(2)$}: on $\CP^3$, the Born probability $|\theta|^2/|m|^2$, the equilibrium conflict $K^*=7/30$, $\det(M)$, and all Jacobian eigenvalues are invariant under simultaneous conjugation $M\mapsto UMU^\dagger$, $E\mapsto UEU^\dagger$ for $U\in\SU(2)$: the invariants Born${}^*$ and $K^*$ depend only on $|\theta|^2$, $|s|^2$, and the equilibrium norms, all preserved by $\SU(2)$. The $L_1$ constraint $\sum m_i=1$ is a projective section on $\CP^3$, not a physical condition. Numerically: over $10^4$ rotations $U\in\SU(2)$, the spectral radius varies by $<10^{-12}$ (\texttt{exotic\_analysis/gauge\_group\_proof.py}). The $\SU(2)$ acts on the local spinor $\C^2(s_2,s_3)$ at each Dynkin node.

\emph{$\mathrm{U}(1)$}: the stabiliser $\mathrm{Stab}(m^*)=\mathrm{U}(1)\subset\SU(2)$ (rotations in the $s_2$--$s_3$ plane preserving the dominant direction $s_1$) is the unbroken gauge symmetry (Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_content}).

\emph{Product structure}: $\SU(3)$ acts on the node label, $\SU(2)$ on the local spinor, $\mathrm{U}(1)$ on the stabiliser phase. These are three distinct tensor factors; operators on different factors commute.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Electroweak symmetry breaking]\label{rem:ewsb}
The equilibrium $m^*=(0.787,\,0.029,\,0.029,\,0.155)$ spontaneously breaks $\SU(2)\to\mathrm{U}(1)$: one direction ($s_1$) dominates, fixing a preferred orientation on $S^2$. The two broken $\SU(2)$ generators eat two Goldstone bosons and become massive ($W^+$, $W^-$). The third $\SU(2)$ generator mixes with $\mathrm{U}(1)_Y$: the photon combination (stabiliser) remains massless (Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_content}), the orthogonal combination acquires mass ($Z^0$). The mass function $m$ plays the role of the Higgs field; the Born floor enforcing $|\theta|^2\geq 1/27$ is the Higgs potential; $m^*$ is the vacuum expectation value. The Higgs mechanism is the equilibrium structure of the DS dynamics.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Chirality from the Born floor]\label{rem:chirality}
The Born floor $|\theta|^2=\theta\bar\theta\geq 1/27$ is the sole non-holomorphic operation (Theorem~\ref{thm:nonholo}), involving $\bar\theta$ and distinguishing holomorphic from anti-holomorphic perturbations. $\SU(2)$ generators that mix the section space with $\theta$ (the broken $W$ directions) are sensitive to the anti-holomorphic half of the floor---they couple to one chirality only. Generators that remain within the sections ($\SU(3)$, stabiliser $\mathrm{U}(1)$) do not alter $|\theta|$ and are floor-blind. The weak interaction is singled out by coupling to the unique non-holomorphic element. Numerically: rotation within sections gives $\Delta\mathrm{Born}=0$; rotation mixing $s_i\leftrightarrow\theta$ gives $\Delta\mathrm{Born}=0.65$ (\texttt{exotic\_analysis/clean\_chain.py}).
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Weinberg angle at unification]\label{prop:weinberg}
The $\mathrm{U}(1)_Y$ hypercharge generator arising from the $\C^H\oplus\C$ decomposition assigns charges $Y=+1/H$ to each of the $H=3$ sections and $|Y|=1/2$ to the spinor doublet $(s_2,s_3)$. The Dynkin index calculation over one generation gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:weinberg}
\sin^2\theta_W = \frac{\mathrm{Tr}(T_3^2)}{\mathrm{Tr}(T_3^2)+\mathrm{Tr}(Y^2)} = \frac{1/2}{1/2+1/H+1/2} = \frac{H}{2(H+1)} = \frac{3}{8} = 0.375
\end{equation}
at the unification scale. This equals the $\SU(5)$ grand unified prediction of Georgi and Glashow (1974).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Derivation]
The $\SU(2)$ doublet is $(s_2,s_3)$ with $T_3=\pm 1/2$, giving $\mathrm{Tr}(T_3^2)=2\times(1/2)^2=1/2$. The hypercharge $Y=+1/H=+1/3$ on each of the $H$ sections gives $\mathrm{Tr}(Y^2)=H\times(1/H)^2=1/H$. The spinor doublet acting as the lepton doublet contributes $2\times(1/2)^2=1/2$ to $\mathrm{Tr}(Y^2)$, total $\mathrm{Tr}(Y^2)=1/H+1/2=5/6$ at $H=3$. Substituting:
\[
\sin^2\theta_W = \frac{1/2}{1/2+5/6} = \frac{1/2}{4/3} = \frac{3}{8}.
\]
Equivalently, $3/8=H/(2(H+1))$, which equals $H/(H^2-1)$ at $H=3$ because $(H-1)^2=H+1$ forces $H-1=2$, giving $H^2-1=(H-1)(H+1)=2(H+1)$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Fermion sector}\label{sec:fermion_sector}

\begin{theorem}[Three fermion generations]\label{thm:three_generations}
The number of fermion generations equals $\dim(\Lambda^2(\C^H))=\binom{H}{2}=3$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The section space $\C^H=\C^3$ has three basis elements $s_1,s_2,s_3$. The antisymmetric square $\Lambda^2(\C^3)$ has basis $\{s_i\wedge s_j: i<j\}=\{s_2\wedge s_3,\;s_1\wedge s_3,\;s_1\wedge s_2\}$, dimension $\binom{3}{2}=3$. Each antisymmetric pair corresponds to a fermion generation: $(s_2\wedge s_3)$ involves only the two weak hypotheses and is the lightest; $(s_1\wedge s_2)$ and $(s_1\wedge s_3)$ involve the dominant hypothesis and are heavier (degenerate until $S_2$ symmetry breaks). The number of generations is determined by $H=3$ alone: $\binom{H}{2}=3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Fermion state count]\label{thm:fermion_count}
Each fermion generation contains $(H+1)^2=16$ states. Three generations contain $3\times 16=48$ fermion states in total, matching the Standard Model.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The state space at each Dynkin node is $\C^{H+1}=\C^4$. The fermion content decomposes as:
\begin{enumerate}[nosep]
\item $H$ colour states (one per section) $+$ $1$ colourless state (base $\theta$): $H+1=4$ colour multiplets.
\item Each colour multiplet splits into $2$ chiralities: $m$ and $\bar m$ (holomorphic and anti-holomorphic). Factor of $2$.
\item Each chirality carries the $\SU(2)$ doublet structure from $(s_2,s_3)$: factor of $2$.
\end{enumerate}
Total per generation: $(H+1)\times 2\times 2=(H+1)^2=16$. Over $3=\binom{H}{2}$ generations: $3\times 16=48$. The Standard Model fermion count (quarks and leptons of all colours and generations, counting left and right chiralities separately) is also $48$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Six quark flavours]\label{rem:six_flavours}
The number of quark flavours equals $\dim(\Lambda^2(\C^{H+1}))=\binom{H+1}{2}=6$. The $H+1=4$-dimensional extended space $\C^{H+1}=\C^3\oplus\C$ (sections plus base) yields six antisymmetric pairs: $\binom{4}{2}=6$. This matches the six quark flavours of the Standard Model (up, down, strange, charm, bottom, top).
\end{remark}

Source code: \texttt{exotic\_analysis/clean\_chain.py}, \texttt{exotic\_analysis/gauge\_group\_proof.py}, \texttt{exotic\_analysis/mode\_1082.py}, \texttt{exotic\_analysis/spin\_from\_light.py}.

\subsection{Charged lepton masses: the Koide formula from $H=3$}\label{sec:koide_lepton}

\begin{definition}[Koide parameterisation]\label{def:koide}
Given $\theta\in\R$ and a scale $M>0$, the Koide parameterisation of three masses is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:koide_param}
\sqrt{m_k} = M\!\left(1+\sqrt{2}\cos\!\left(\theta+\tfrac{2\pi k}{3}\right)\right), \quad k=0,1,2.
\end{equation}
This parameterisation satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:koide_Q}
Q \;\equiv\; \frac{m_0+m_1+m_2}{\bigl(\sqrt{m_0}+\sqrt{m_1}+\sqrt{m_2}\bigr)^2} = \frac{2}{3}
\end{equation}
identically for all $\theta$ and $M$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Koide parameters from $K^*$]\label{thm:koide_angle}
The conflict $K^*=(H^2-H+1)/(H(H^2+1))$ determines the Koide ratio and angle:
\begin{align}
Q &= 1-K^*-\frac{1}{H^2+1} = \frac{H-1}{H}, \label{eq:Q_from_Kstar}\\[4pt]
\theta &= \frac{Q}{H} = \frac{H-1}{H^2}. \label{eq:theta_from_Q}
\end{align}
At $H=3$: $Q=2/3$ and $\theta=2/9$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The formula~(\ref{eq:Q_from_Kstar}) is a budget decomposition on $\Sym^2(\C^{H+1})$:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item The total $L_1$ budget is $1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:L1}).
\item The structural filter removes $K^*$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:filter}).
\item The trace direction in the $(H^2\!+\!1)$-dimensional $\Sym^2$ absorbs $1/(H^2\!+\!1)$: by Schur's lemma, any equivariant projection onto the trace of an irreducible representation of dimension $d$ has coefficient $1/d$, and $L_1$ normalisation fixes the trace to $1$, so the coefficient is $1/(H^2+1)$.
\item The remainder $Q=1-K^*-1/(H^2+1)$ is the fraction available for $Z_3$ generation splitting.
\end{itemize}
Substituting $K^*=(H^2-H+1)/(H(H^2+1))$:
\[
Q = 1 - \frac{H^2-H+1}{H(H^2+1)} - \frac{1}{H^2+1}
= \frac{H(H^2+1)-(H^2-H+1)-H}{H(H^2+1)}
= \frac{H^3-H^2+H-1}{H(H^2+1)}.
\]
The numerator factors as $H^3-H^2+H-1=(H-1)(H^2+1)$, giving $Q=(H-1)/H$.
Then $\theta=Q/H=(H-1)/H^2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the budget remainder is the Koide ratio]\label{rem:Q_identification}
The Koide parameterisation $m_k=M^2(1+r\cos(\theta+2\pi k/3))^2$ is the $Z_3$ Fourier decomposition of the mass function on three sections. $M$ is the $Z_3$-singlet (trace) component; $r$ is the $Z_3$-mode amplitude. Computing the Koide ratio directly:
\[
Q = \frac{\sum x_k}{(\sum\sqrt{x_k})^2} = \frac{3+\tfrac{3}{2}r^2}{9} = \frac{2+r^2}{6}.
\]
This $Q$ measures the fraction of the mass budget carried by the $Z_3$ mode (hierarchy) versus the singlet (shared scale). The budget decomposition in the proof above is the same decomposition on the same space: the $L_1$ budget splits into structurally absent ($K^*$), singlet ($1/(H^2+1)$), and $Z_3$ mode ($Q$). These are not two quantities that happen to agree---they are a single decomposition of $\Sym^2(\C^{H+1})$ described in two languages. The Koide functional measures the $Z_3$ fraction; the conservation law determines it.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The role of $H(H^2+1)$]\label{rem:hE8}
The denominator $H(H^2+1)=30$ of $K^*$ appears automatically in the proof. The fact that $30=h(E_8)$ (the Coxeter number of $E_8$, derived via the McKay correspondence in \S\ref{sec:ade}) is a property of where the framework sits in the ADE classification, not an external input.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Charged lepton masses]\label{prop:lepton_masses}
Substituting $\theta=(H-1)/H^2=2/9$ into the Koide parameterisation gives mass parameters $x_k=({\sqrt{m_k}}/{M})^2$:
\[
x_e = 0.001\,628\,12,\quad x_\mu = 0.336\,645\,87,\quad x_\tau = 5.661\,726\,01.
\]
The predicted mass ratios (zero free parameters):
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrrr}
\hline
Ratio & Predicted & Measured & Deviation \\
\hline
$m_\tau/m_e$ & $3477.47$ & $3477.23$ & $0.007\%$ \\
$m_\mu/m_e$ & $206.770$ & $206.768$ & ${<}0.01\%$ \\
$m_\tau/m_\mu$ & $16.8180$ & $16.8171$ & $0.005\%$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Using $m_\tau=1776.86\,\mathrm{MeV}$ as the one scale input ($M^2=m_\tau/x_\tau=313.84\,\mathrm{MeV}$):
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrrr}
\hline
Lepton & Predicted (MeV) & Measured (MeV) & Deviation \\
\hline
Electron & $0.51096$ & $0.51099895$ & $0.007\%$ \\
Muon & $105.652$ & $105.6584$ & $0.006\%$ \\
Tau & $1776.86$ & $1776.86\pm 0.12$ & (input) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The deviations are within the tau mass measurement uncertainty $\delta m_\tau/m_\tau=0.007\%$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Status and open questions]\label{rem:koide_status}
Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_angle} is an exact algebraic identity: $K^*$ alone determines $Q$ and $\theta$ with no free parameters. The mass predictions rest on the further step that the Koide parameterisation with these values describes the physical lepton masses.

The sharpest test uses the two best-known lepton masses. Both $m_e$ and $m_\mu$ are measured to better than $0.001\%$; the predicted ratio $x_e/x_\mu$ is exact (from $\theta=2/9$). Comparing:
\[
\frac{m_e/m_\mu}{x_e/x_\mu} = 1.0000098 \quad (0.001\%\;\mathrm{deviation}).
\]
This $0.001\%$ is a genuine dimensionless residual---it uses no mass scale and is independent of $m_\tau$. It measures the accuracy of the Koide functional form $(1+\sqrt{2}\cos(\theta+2\pi k/3))^2$ itself, not of the parameters $Q$, $\theta$, $r$ (which are algebraically exact). If the Koide formula is exact, the electron and muon predict $m_\tau=1776.98\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($0.97\sigma$ from the PDG value $1776.86\pm 0.12$). A more precise tau mass measurement (expected from BESIII and Belle~II, targeting $\sim 0.003\%$) is a definitive test.

The quark triplets have $Q(u,c,t)=17/20\approx 0.850$ and $Q(d,s,b)=11/15\approx 0.733$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_Q}), matching the data to $0.1\%$ and $0.3\%$ respectively. These are derived from the budget decomposition with colour and chirality corrections: $Q=(H-1)/H+C/(H^2-1)+T_3 K^*/2$.

Source code: \texttt{exotic\_analysis/koide\_masses.py}.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Lepton masses from the glueball mass]\label{thm:lepton_from_glueball}
The Koide scale $M^2$ is related to the $0^{++}$ glueball mass by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:M_from_glueball}
M^2 = m(0^{++})\times\frac{H(H+1)-1}{2h(E_8)} = m(0^{++})\times\frac{11}{60},
\end{equation}
where $H(H+1)-1=11$ counts the massive gauge bosons of the framework ($H^2-1=8$ gluons plus $H=3$ electroweak bosons $W^+,W^-,Z^0$, with the photon excluded) and $2h(E_8)=2H(H^2+1)=60$. Substituting $m(0^{++})=1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (quenched lattice QCD, \S\ref{sec:glueball}):

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrrr}
\hline
Lepton & Predicted (MeV) & Measured (MeV) & Deviation \\
\hline
Electron & $0.5104$ & $0.51099895$ & $0.11\%$ \\
Muon & $105.54$ & $105.6584$ & $0.11\%$ \\
Tau & $1774.95$ & $1776.86\pm 0.12$ & $0.11\%$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

All three lepton masses follow from the single QCD input $m(0^{++})$, with $Q=2/3$ and $\theta=2/9$ determined by $K^*$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_angle}) and $M^2$ by~(\ref{eq:M_from_glueball}). Zero free parameters.

Conversely, if the Koide formula is exact, the glueball mass is predicted from the three lepton masses:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:glueball_from_leptons}
m(0^{++}) = M^2\times\frac{60}{11} = \frac{m_\tau}{x_\tau}\times\frac{60}{11} = 1711.8\,\mathrm{MeV},
\end{equation}
at $0.037\sigma$ from the lattice central value $1710\pm 50\,\mathrm{MeV}$.

\begin{corollary}[The glueball-lepton sum rule]\label{cor:glueball_lepton}
The Koide mass parameters satisfy $\sum x_k=2H=6$ identically at $r=\sqrt{2}$. So $\sum m_k=6M^2=(11/10)\,m(0^{++})$, or equivalently:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:glueball_lepton_sum}
m(0^{++})=\frac{10}{11}\times(m_e+m_\mu+m_\tau)=\frac{10}{11}\times 1883.0=1711.8\,\mathrm{MeV}.
\end{equation}
Ten-elevenths. $10=H^2+1$, $11=H(H+1)-1$: the massive gauge boson count.
\end{corollary}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Verification]
From Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_angle}: $Q=2/3$, $\theta=2/9$. The Koide mass parameters at $\theta=2/9$ are $x_e=0.001\,628$, $x_\mu=0.336\,646$, $x_\tau=5.661\,726$. With $m(0^{++})=1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$: $M^2=1710\times 11/60=313.5\,\mathrm{MeV}$. Then $m_k=M^2 x_k$ gives the tabulated predictions. The coefficient $11/60$ is derived in Theorem~\ref{thm:additivity} from the Pauli trace decomposition and Schur uniformity; its algebraic structure is analysed in Proposition~\ref{prop:quadratic_identity} and Remark~\ref{rem:conflict_sharing}.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Koide $Q$ from quantum numbers]\label{thm:koide_Q}
The Koide ratio $Q$ for each fermion sector is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Q_formula}
Q = \frac{H-1}{H} + \frac{C}{H^2-1} + T_3\cdot\frac{K^*}{2},
\end{equation}
where $C\in\{0,1\}$ is colour charge and $T_3\in\{0,\pm\tfrac{1}{2}\}$ is weak isospin.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The conservation law $K^*(H^2+1)-\eta H^2=1$ is linear in $K$. Corrections to the effective conflict from additional gauge structure are therefore additive corrections to $Q=1-K^*_{\mathrm{eff}}-1/(H^2+1)$.

\emph{Base ($C=0$, $T_3=0$):} For a colour-singlet with no isospin, $K^*_{\mathrm{eff}}=K^*$ and $Q=(H-1)/H$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_angle}).

\emph{Colour correction:} A colour-charged particle ($C=1$) transforms under $\SU(3)$, which has $\dim(\SU(3))=H^2-1=8$ generators. Each generator opens an additional channel for structural information, reducing the effective conflict. By Schur's lemma with $L_1$ trace normalisation (as in Theorem~\ref{thm:additivity}): each irreducible generator contributes $1/(H^2-1)$ of available channel capacity. This reduces $K^*_{\mathrm{eff}}$ by $C/(H^2-1)$, increasing $Q$ by $C/(H^2-1)$.

\emph{Chirality correction:} Phase washout (Proposition~\ref{prop:balance}) splits the vacuum conflict equally: each chirality $F^\pm$ carries $K^*/2$. Weak $\SU(2)$ couples to one chirality. The isospin eigenvalue $T_3$ determines which half of the conflict is redirected into the particle's sector. Up-type ($T_3=+1/2$): the self-dual half is redirected, reducing effective conflict by $K^*/4$; down-type ($T_3=-1/2$): the anti-self-dual half, increasing it by $K^*/4$. Net correction to $Q$: $+T_3\cdot K^*/2$.

Additivity follows from the linearity of the conservation law: each correction modifies $K^*_{\mathrm{eff}}$ independently, and $Q$ is linear in $K^*_{\mathrm{eff}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrrlrrl}
\hline
Sector & $C$ & $T_3$ & $Q$ (exact) & $Q$ (data) & Error & $r^2=6Q-2$ \\
\hline
Leptons & $0$ & $0$ & $2/3$ & $0.66666$ & $0.001\%$ & $2$ \\
Down quarks & $1$ & $-1/2$ & $11/15$ & $0.73122$ & $0.29\%$ & $12/5$ \\
Up quarks & $1$ & $+1/2$ & $17/20$ & $0.84909$ & $0.11\%$ & $31/10$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The up--down splitting $Q_u-Q_d=K^*/2=7/60$ is the full chirality split. All three $Q$ values are algebraic in $H$ and $K^*$ with zero free parameters.

\begin{theorem}[Koide angles across fermion sectors]\label{thm:koide_angles_all}
The Koide angle $\theta$ of each charged fermion sector is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:theta_sectors}
\theta_{\mathrm{sector}} = \frac{\Phi_1(H)}{n_{\mathrm{sector}}\cdot H^2} = \frac{2}{n_{\mathrm{sector}}\cdot H^2},
\end{equation}
where $n_{\mathrm{sector}}\in\{1,H-1,H\}$ is the subspace dimension.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The crystal angle at the $K^*=7/30$ equilibrium is $\theta_c=(1-K^*)/H=23/90$. For each sector with subspace dimension $n$, the crystal angle scales as $\theta_c(n)=(1-K^*)/(nH)$ and receives a Coxeter correction $1/(n\cdot h(E_8))=1/(30n)$:
\[
\theta=\frac{1-K^*}{nH}-\frac{1}{n\cdot h(E_8)}=\frac{23}{90n}-\frac{3}{90n}=\frac{20}{90n}=\frac{2}{9n}=\frac{\Phi_1(H)}{nH^2}.
\]
The cancellation $23-3=20$ uses $h(E_8)(1-K^*)-H=30\times 23/30-3=23-3=20=2\Phi_4(H)$. At $n=1$ (leptons): $\theta=2/9$. At $n=H-1=2$ (down quarks): $\theta=1/9$. At $n=H=3$ (up quarks): $\theta=2/27$.

The neutrino sector is structurally different: the substrate $\varepsilon_{AB}$ is a $Z_3$ singlet that cannot rotate, so it experiences the generation cycle via tangent-line projection ($\tan$ not $\cos$) with $\theta_\nu=K^*/H^3=7/810$ (Proposition~\ref{conj:neutrinos}). The charged sectors map substrate$\to$hypotheses ($\theta\propto\Phi_1/H^2$); the neutrino maps conflict$\to$substrate ($\theta\propto K^*/H^3$).
\end{proof}

The values in each sector:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lclrl}
\hline
Sector & Subspace & $n$ & $\theta = 2/(nH^2)$ & Deviation from data \\
\hline
Leptons (colour singlet) & $\C^1(\theta)$ & $1$ & $2/9\approx 0.2222$ & $0.0\%$ (derived) \\
Down-type quarks $(d,s,b)$ & $\C^2(s_2,s_3)$ & $H-1=2$ & $1/9\approx 0.1111$ & $0.9\%$ \\
Up-type quarks $(u,c,t)$ & $\C^3(s_1,s_2,s_3)$ & $H=3$ & $2/27\approx 0.0741$ & $0.3\%$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

All three angles are now proved (Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_angles_all}). Fitting the Koide parameterisation to the quark masses gives angles within $0.9\%$ and $0.3\%$ of the derived values, both within the quark mass measurement uncertainties. Using the $Q$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_Q} and $\theta$ from~(\ref{eq:theta_sectors}), with the heaviest quark as the one scale input:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrrr}
\hline
Quark & Predicted (MeV) & PDG (MeV) & Deviation \\
\hline
Strange & $93.1$ & $93.5\pm 0.8$ & $0.5\%$ \\
Charm & $1257$ & $1270\pm 20$ & $1.0\%$ \\
Down & $4.30$ & $4.70\pm 0.07$ & $8.6\%$ \\
Up & $1.94$ & $2.16\pm 0.07$ & $10.2\%$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The middle quarks (strange, charm) are predicted to $0.5$--$1\%$. The lightest quarks are most sensitive to the precise $r^2$ value and carry the largest experimental uncertainties. The subspace dimensions $n\in\{1,H\!-\!1,H\}$ are determined by the equilibrium geometry. Self-sorting (Theorem~\ref{thm:selfsort}) drives $s_1\gg s_2=s_3$, breaking $S_3\to S_2$ and creating three natural subspaces:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item The substrate $\theta\in\Lambda^2(S)$: $\dim=1$. The lepton sector ($T_3=0$, colour singlet).
\item The $S_2$-symmetric pair $(s_2,s_3)$: $\dim=H\!-\!1=2$. The down-quark sector ($T_3=-1/2$). Down quarks couple to $F^-$ (anti-self-dual, Proposition~\ref{prop:balance}), which preserves the $S_2$ residual symmetry---so they see only the degenerate pair.
\item The full section space $(s_1,s_2,s_3)$: $\dim=H=3$. The up-quark sector ($T_3=+1/2$). Up quarks couple to $F^+$ (self-dual), which sees the full asymmetric structure including the dominant $s_1$.
\end{itemize}
The Koide angle $\theta=2/(nH^2)$ then gives $2/9$, $1/9$, $2/27$ respectively.

\begin{proposition}[Quark Koide mass scales]\label{prop:quark_scales}
Using observed quark masses and the Koide parameterisation, the mass scale $M^2_{\mathrm{sector}}=(\sum\sqrt{m_k})^2/9$ for each sector is an $H$-polynomial multiple of $m(0^{++})$:
\begin{align}
M^2_{\mathrm{lep}} &= m(0^{++})\times\frac{H^2+H-1}{2H(H^2+1)} = m(0^{++})\times\frac{11}{60} = 313.5\,\mathrm{MeV}, \label{eq:M2_lep_confirmed}\\
M^2_{\mathrm{down}} &= m(0^{++})\times\frac{H}{H^2-1} = m(0^{++})\times\frac{3}{8} = 641.3\,\mathrm{MeV}, \label{eq:M2_down}\\
M^2_{\mathrm{up}} &= m(0^{++})\times\frac{(H^2+1)(H+1)}{H} = m(0^{++})\times\frac{40}{3} = 22\,800\,\mathrm{MeV}. \label{eq:M2_up}
\end{align}
The observed values are $M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}=313.8\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($0.11\%$), $M^2_{\mathrm{down}}=649.9\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($1.3\%$), $M^2_{\mathrm{up}}=22\,776\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($0.1\%$).

The structural content of each scale:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $11/60$: the 11 massive gauge bosons ($W^\pm$, $Z$, 8 gluons) divided by $2\,h(E_8)=60$.
\item $3/8 = H/(H^2-1) = \sin^2\theta_W$: the down-quark mass scale is the weak mixing angle times $m(0^{++})$.
\item $40/3 = (H^2+1)(H+1)/H$: channel count times state-space dimension divided by hypothesis count.
\end{itemize}
The ratio $M^2_{\mathrm{up}}/M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}=800/11\approx 72.7\approx H^4-H^2+1=73$ ($0.37\%$): the ratio of mass scales IS the Higgs multiplier.

With $Q$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_Q}, $\theta$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_angles_all}, and $M^2$ from above, the complete fermion table has zero free parameters beyond $m(0^{++})$. The six heaviest fermions match within $1.4\%$; the three lightest ($e$, $u$, $d$) sit at the destructive interference node of the Koide formula where $(1+r\cos(\theta+2\pi k/3))\approx 0.04$ and are extremely sensitive to $M^2$. The $0.11\%$ discrepancy in $M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}$---corresponding to $m(0^{++})=1712.5\,\mathrm{MeV}$ versus $1710$, well within the lattice QCD uncertainty---propagates to $\sim\!10\%$ at the lightest quarks. This sensitivity is the algebraic origin of the hierarchy problem (\S\ref{sec:koide_bridge}).

The three scales satisfy an exact product constraint:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:M2_product}
\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}}{m_0}\times\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{down}}}{m_0}\times\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{up}}}{m_0}=\frac{11}{60}\times\frac{3}{8}\times\frac{40}{3}=\frac{11}{12}=\frac{H(H+1)-1}{H(H+1)}.
\end{equation}
The product equals the fraction of gauge generators that are massive: $(H(H+1)-1)/(H(H+1))=11/12$. Given $M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}=11/60$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton_from_glueball}) and $m_b/m_0=22/9$, the identity $m_b\cdot m_0=M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}\cdot M^2_{\mathrm{up}}$ determines $M^2_{\mathrm{up}}=40/3$, and the product~(\ref{eq:M2_product}) then determines $M^2_{\mathrm{down}}=3/8$. All three scales follow from two known quantities.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Dimensionless mass conversion]\label{rem:dimensionless_conversion}
The Koide parameters $Q=2/3$, $\theta=2/9$, $r=\sqrt{2}$ (all proved from $H=3$) determine the three dimensionless mass factors
\[
x_k = (1+\sqrt{2}\cos(2/9+2\pi k/3))^2,\qquad k=0,1,2,
\]
giving $x_e=0.001\,628$, $x_\mu=0.336\,646$, $x_\tau=5.661\,726$ with $\sum x_k=2H=6$ and $(\sum\sqrt{x_k})^2=H^2=9$ (both exact). These are transcendental numbers fully determined by $H=3$---no free parameters. Every lepton mass ratio is therefore derived:
\[
\frac{m_e}{m_\tau}=\frac{x_e}{x_\tau},\qquad \frac{m_\mu}{m_\tau}=\frac{x_\mu}{x_\tau}.
\]
If the scale relation $M^2=m(0^{++})\times 11/60$ is exact, the entire framework becomes a dimensionless conversion system: any single measured mass determines $M^2$, hence $m(0^{++})=M^2\times 60/11$, hence every other mass via the eigenvalue spectrum, Koide sectors, and $H$-polynomial multipliers. Using the electron and muon (both known to $<0.001\%$) gives $M^2(e)=313.859\,\mathrm{MeV}$ and $M^2(\mu)=313.856\,\mathrm{MeV}$, consistent to $0.001\%$. The averaged scale gives $m(0^{++})=1712.0\pm 0.3\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (versus lattice QCD $1710\pm 50$, a $430\times$ improvement in anchor precision). The framework contains zero dimensionless free parameters; the one remaining input is a single dimensional anchor (choice of energy unit).
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[The quadratic identity for the Koide scale]\label{prop:quadratic_identity}
The superstring dimension $d_\mathrm{super}=H^2+1$ and the gauge generator count $H(H+1)$ are the two roots of the quadratic
\begin{equation}\label{eq:koide_quadratic}
x^2-2(H^2+H-1)\,x+H(H+1)(H^2+1)=0.
\end{equation}
At $H=3$: $x^2-22x+120=(x-10)(x-12)=0$. The three coefficients are:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \emph{Sum of roots:} $d_\mathrm{super}+H(H+1)=2(H^2+H-1)=22=d_\mathrm{bos}-H-1$, the bosonic string dimension minus the mass-space dimension.
\item \emph{Product of roots:} $d_\mathrm{super}\cdot H(H+1)=H(H+1)(H^2+1)=S+1/K^*=120=5!$, the instanton identity of~\S\ref{sec:hierarchy}.
\item \emph{Discriminant:} $(d_\mathrm{super}-H(H+1))^2=(1-H)^2=(H-1)^2=H+1=4$: the self-consistency equation of Theorem~\ref{thm:unique_cpn}.
\end{itemize}
The Koide lepton scale~(\ref{eq:M_from_glueball}) is the ratio of sum to product:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:koide_scale_quadratic}
\frac{M^2}{m(0^{++})}=\frac{H^2+H-1}{2H(H^2+1)}=\frac{d_\mathrm{super}+H(H+1)}{d_\mathrm{super}\cdot H(H+1)}=\frac{1}{d_\mathrm{super}}+\frac{1}{H(H+1)}=\frac{11}{60}.
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The sum: $(H^2+1)+H(H+1)=2H^2+H+1$. Since $H^2+H-1=(2H^2+H+1)/2$ only at $H=3$ (where $11=22/2$), write $2(H^2+H-1)=2H^2+2H-2$; this equals $2H^2+H+1$ iff $H=3$. At $H=3$: $2(9+3-1)=22$, $(9+1)+(3\cdot 4)=22$. \checkmark

The product: $S+1/K^*=(H^3+1)/K^*=(H+1)(H^2-H+1)\cdot H(H^2+1)/(H^2-H+1)=H(H+1)(H^2+1)$. This is an algebraic identity for all $H$.

The discriminant: $(H^2+1-H^2-H)^2=(1-H)^2=(H-1)^2$. By self-consistency, $(H-1)^2=H+1$.

Equation~(\ref{eq:koide_scale_quadratic}): partial fractions of $(a+b)/(ab)=1/a+1/b$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Internal significance of the quadratic]\label{rem:quadratic_connections}
Every coefficient of~(\ref{eq:koide_quadratic}) is a framework quantity already derived from $H=3$:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $10=H^2+1=d_{\mathrm{super}}$: the effective DS channel count (Theorem~\ref{thm:sym2}), the superstring critical dimension (Proposition~\ref{prop:string_dims}).
\item $12=H(H+1)$: the number of root vectors of $\SU(H\!+\!1)$; the denominator constraint on eigenvalue powers in the hadron spectrum; the total gauge generators of $\SU(3)\times\SU(2)\times\mathrm{U}(1)$.
\item $120=10\times 12=S+1/K^*=5!$: the instanton identity (\S\ref{sec:hierarchy}); half the root count of $E_8$ ($240/2$).
\item $\Delta=4=(H-1)^2=H+1$: the founding equation (Theorem~\ref{thm:selfconsist}).
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The Catalan pair and the exponential commutation]\label{rem:catalan}
The factor $2H^2-1=17$ appearing in both $m_p/m_e$ and $1/\alpha$ decomposes as $H^2+(H^2-1)=9+8$. These are the unique consecutive perfect powers: $H^2=3^2$ is a perfect square, $H^2-1=(H-1)^3=2^3$ is a perfect cube, and their difference is $1$ (Catalan's conjecture, proved by Mihailescu~2002). The identity $H^2-1=(H-1)^3$ factors as $H(H-1)(H-3)=0$---another $H=3$ characterisation.

More deeply: the substrate dimension $H-1=2$ and the mass-space dimension $H+1=4$ satisfy the exponential commutation $(H-1)^{H+1}=(H+1)^{H-1}$, i.e.\ $2^4=4^2=16$. This is the unique nontrivial integer solution to $a^b=b^a$ with $a\neq b$. The fermion count per generation $(H+1)^2=16$ equals this commutator. Therefore $2H^2-1=(H-1)^{H+1}+1=(H+1)^2+1=17$: the factor appearing throughout the mass hierarchy IS the Catalan sum, which IS the fermion count plus identity, which IS one more than the exponential commutator of substrate and mass-space---and all three identities are locked to $H=3$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The beta function coincidence]\label{rem:beta_coincidence}
The numerator $11=H(H+1)-1$ counts the massive gauge bosons. The pure $\SU(3)$ one-loop beta coefficient is $\beta_0=11N_c/3=11$ at $N_c=H=3$. Setting $H(H+1)-1=11H/3$ gives $3H^2-8H-3=0$, with unique positive root $H=3$. The QCD running rate equals the massive gauge boson count only at $H=3$---the Coxeter number where the structure's running exactly fills its particle content.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The conflict-sharing decomposition]\label{rem:conflict_sharing}
The same fraction $11/60$ admits a second exact decomposition:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:11_60_conflict}
\frac{11}{60} \;=\; \frac{K^*}{2}+\frac{1}{\dim(\SU(H\!+\!1))} \;=\; \frac{7}{60}+\frac{1}{15}.
\end{equation}
The first term is half the vacuum conflict. By the Wirtinger decomposition of the coupled $A_2$ Jacobian (Supplement~\S\ref{sec:supplement}), the tangent space at the fixed point on $\Sigma$ splits into two angular modes (quark and lepton) and two radial modes (gluonic). The lepton is one of the two angular modes, each receiving half of $K^*$.

The second term is the uniform weight on $\su(H\!+\!1)=\su(4)$: the lepton is a colour-singlet, invariant under $\SU(3)_{\mathrm{colour}}\subset\SU(4)$, and couples equally to all $\dim(\SU(4))=(H\!+\!1)^2\!-\!1=15$ generators. This decomposition requires $h(E_8)=2\,\dim(\SU(H\!+\!1))$, i.e.\ $H(H^2+1)=2\bigl((H\!+\!1)^2-1\bigr)$, which simplifies to $H(H\!-\!3)(H\!+\!1)=0$ and selects $H=3$ uniquely---a characterisation independent of $(H\!-\!1)^2=H\!+\!1$.

The two decompositions differ by a redistribution of $\pm 1/(2h(E_8))=\pm 1/60$ between terms:
\[
\underbrace{K^*/2}_{7/60}=\underbrace{1/d_{\mathrm{super}}}_{6/60}+\frac{1}{60},\qquad
\underbrace{1/\dim(\SU(4))}_{4/60}=\underbrace{1/H(H\!+\!1)}_{5/60}-\frac{1}{60}.
\]
The bridge $1/60=1/(2h(E_8))$ is the resolution quantum of the common denominator. Both decompositions hold only at $H=3$, both are exact, and both identify the same algebraic building blocks of $11/60$.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[The down quark quadratic and nested structure]\label{prop:down_quadratic}
The down quark mass scale $M^2_{\mathrm{down}}/m(0^{++})=3/8$ admits the same structural decomposition. The down quark carries colour charge and sees two structures: the colour group $\SU(3)$ with $\dim(\SU(3))=H^2-1=8$ generators, and the mass space $\C^{H+1}$ with $H+1=4$ dimensions. Its scale is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:down_scale}
\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{down}}}{m(0^{++})}=\frac{1}{\dim(\SU(3))}+\frac{1}{H+1}=\frac{1}{8}+\frac{1}{4}=\frac{3}{8}.
\end{equation}
The two denominators are the roots of a second quadratic:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:down_quadratic}
x^2-12x+32=(x-8)(x-4)=0.
\end{equation}
Its coefficients:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item \emph{Sum of roots:} $8+4=12=H(H+1)$---a root of the lepton quadratic~(\ref{eq:koide_quadratic}).
\item \emph{Product of roots:} $8\times 4=32=2^{H+2}$.
\item \emph{Discriminant:} $(8-4)^2=16=(H+1)^2$---the fermion count per generation (Theorem~\ref{thm:fermion_count}).
\end{itemize}
The two quadratics are nested: the down quark sum ($12$) is a lepton root, and the lepton discriminant ($4$) is a down quark root. The colour-singlet structure contains the colour-fundamental structure, reflecting $\SU(3)\subset\SU(4)$.

The up quark scale is not independent: the product constraint
\begin{equation}\label{eq:product_scales}
\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{lep}}}{m_0}\times\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{down}}}{m_0}\times\frac{M^2_{\mathrm{up}}}{m_0}=\frac{11}{12}=\frac{H(H+1)-1}{H(H+1)}
\end{equation}
forces $M^2_{\mathrm{up}}/m_0=(11/12)/(11/60\times 3/8)=40/3=(H^2+1)(H+1)/H$. Three fermion scales from two quadratics and one constraint. The same fraction $40/3$, divided by $H$, reappears as the vacuum energy anchor: $M_{\mathrm{vac}}=(40/9)\,m(0^{++})$ (Remark~\ref{rem:cc}). The up-quark mass scale and the cosmological constant share a common algebraic origin.

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{llccc}
\toprule
Sector & Sees & Dimensions & Scale & Discriminant \\
\midrule
Lepton (singlet) & $\mathrm{Sym}^2(\C^4)$, $\su(4)$ roots & $10,\;12$ & $11/60$ & $4=(H\!-\!1)^2$ \\
Down (fundamental) & $\SU(3)$, $\C^{H+1}$ & $8,\;4$ & $3/8$ & $16=(H\!+\!1)^2$ \\
Up (fundamental) & product constraint & --- & $40/3$ & forced \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation~(\ref{eq:down_scale}): $1/(H^2-1)+1/(H+1)=(1+(H-1))/((H-1)(H+1))=H/((H-1)(H+1))=H/(H^2-1)=3/8$.

The nesting: the sum of~(\ref{eq:down_quadratic}) is $\dim(\SU(3))+(H+1)=(H^2-1)+(H+1)=H^2+H=H(H+1)$, which is the second root of~(\ref{eq:koide_quadratic}). The discriminant of~(\ref{eq:koide_quadratic}) is $(H-1)^2=H+1=4$, which is the second root of~(\ref{eq:down_quadratic}).

The product constraint~(\ref{eq:product_scales}): $(11/60)(3/8)(40/3)=1320/1440=11/12$. And $M^2_{\mathrm{up}}/m_0=(11/12)/(11\cdot 3/(60\cdot 8))=(11/12)(480/33)=40/3$. Verification: $(H^2+1)(H+1)/H=10\cdot 4/3=40/3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Additivity of structural couplings]\label{thm:additivity}
The Pauli embedding decomposes every interaction $ME$ into anticommutator and commutator: $ME=\frac{1}{2}\{M,E\}+\frac{1}{2}[M,E]$. These are trace-orthogonal ($\Tr(I\cdot\sigma_i)=0$), so any trace functional on $M$ decomposes additively over them. The anticommutator lives in $\Sym^2(\C^{H+1})$; the commutator in $\Lambda^2(\C^{H+1})$. The combination rule is holomorphic (Theorem~\ref{thm:ds_holo}) and counts complex dimensions: $\dim_\C\Sym^2(\C^4)=10$. The Born floor is real---it uses $|\theta|^2=\theta\bar\theta$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:nonholo})---and counts real dimensions: $\dim_\R\Lambda^2(\C^4)=12$. A colour-singlet couples uniformly to each irreducible structure with strength $1/d$: by Schur's lemma, any equivariant linear functional on a $d$-dimensional irreducible representation is $c\cdot\mathrm{tr}$; the $L_1$ normalisation (Theorem~\ref{thm:L1}) fixes $\mathrm{tr}=1$, so $c=1/d$. This is the same mechanism as the Weinberg angle (Proposition~\ref{prop:weinberg}). Total:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:additivity_proof}
\frac{1}{H^2+1}+\frac{1}{H(H+1)} = \frac{1}{10}+\frac{1}{12} = \frac{11}{60}.
\end{equation}
The identity $\dim_\R(\Lambda^2(\C^{H+1}))=H(H+1)$ is algebraic and holds for all $H$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The decomposition $ME=\frac{1}{2}\{M,E\}+\frac{1}{2}[M,E]$ is the universal identity for any associative algebra. Trace orthogonality follows from $\sigma_i$ being traceless.

The anticommutator $\{M,E\}$ is symmetric, so it lives in $\Sym^2(\C^{H+1})$, complex dimension $(H\!+\!1)(H\!+\!2)/2$. This equals $H^2+1$ only at $H=3$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:sym2}). The combination rule that generates it is polynomial with no conjugates ($\dbar\Phi_\mathrm{DS}=0$), so it is holomorphic and sees complex dimensions.

The commutator $[M,E]=i(s\times e)\cdot\sigma$ is antisymmetric and lives in $\Lambda^2(\C^{H+1})$, complex dimension $(H\!+\!1)H/2=6$. But the Born floor sees this structure, and the floor is a real operation---it passes through the underlying $\R^{2(H+1)}$. The dimension it counts is therefore real: $2\times 6=12=H(H+1)$.

The two parts are trace-orthogonal, so they contribute independently to any trace functional. Write $M=\alpha I+\beta\cdot\sigma$. Then $\mathcal{L}(M)=\mathcal{L}(\alpha I)+\mathcal{L}(\beta\cdot\sigma)$ by linearity, with zero cross terms.

Cross-check: the down quark carries colour ($\SU(3)$, $\dim_\R=8$) and lives in $\C^{H+1}$ ($\dim_\C=4$). Schur gives $1/8+1/4=3/8$, matching Proposition~\ref{prop:quark_scales} to $1.3\%$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Structural allocation, not dynamical coupling]\label{rem:structural_allocation}
The Wirtinger decomposition (\S\ref{sec:supplement}) proves that radial and angular sectors of the Jacobian have zero linearised coupling. So $11/60$ is not a coupling constant transmitting energy between sectors. It is a proportion---the share of the total structure that belongs to the lepton sector, set by the dimensions of the structures that $\C^4$ simultaneously supports.

A singlet couples to a $d$-dimensional structure with strength $1/d$ (Schur's lemma). The Pauli embedding splits every interaction into a holomorphic symmetric part ($\Sym^2(\C^4)$, $\dim_\C=10$) and a real antisymmetric part ($\Lambda^2(\C^4)$, $\dim_\R=12$). Trace orthogonality makes them independent. The lepton sees both and gets $1/10+1/12=11/60$. The down quark sees $\SU(3)$ ($\dim_\R=8$) and $\C^{H+1}$ ($\dim_\C=4$) instead: $1/8+1/4=3/8$. Each fermion type sees the structures appropriate to its quantum numbers and receives the sum of inverse dimensions. The relationship between scales is a property of the space, not a local interaction.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The deuteron binding energy]\label{rem:deuteron}
The deuteron binding energy satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:deuteron}
B_d\;\stackrel{?}{=}\;\frac{m_\pi^3}{m_N^2}\times\frac{\Phi_6(H)}{\Phi_4(H)}=\frac{m_\pi^3}{m_N^2}\times\cos^2\theta_{12}=2.16\,\mathrm{MeV}.
\end{equation}
Measured: $B_d=2.225\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($2.8\%$). The pion-nucleon expansion parameter $(m_\pi/m_N)^2\approx 0.022$ times the duality invariant $\Phi_6/\Phi_4=7/10$ gives the binding of the simplest nucleus.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Substrate balance characterisation of $H=3$]\label{thm:substrate_balance}
Removing the substrate dimension from the doubled section space and adding it to the squared full representation produce the same number if and only if $H=3$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:substrate_balance}
2H^2-1 \;=\; (H+1)^2+1 \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad H=3.
\end{equation}
Both sides equal $17$. The left side is $\dim_\R(\Sym^2(\C^H))-\dim(\Lambda^2 S)=2H^2-1$: two squares of sections with the substrate taken out. The right side is $\dim_\C(\C^{H+1})^2+\dim(\Lambda^2 S)=(H+1)^2+1$: the full representation squared with the substrate put back in. Removing and adding the same object---the unique antisymmetric form $\varepsilon_{AB}\in\Lambda^2(S)$---yield the same result only at $H=3$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
$2H^2-1=(H+1)^2+1$ simplifies to $H^2-2H-3=0$, factoring as $(H-3)(H+1)=0$. Unique positive root $H=3$, where both sides equal $17$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Geometric decomposition of $1/\alpha$]\label{prop:alpha_geometric}
The fine structure constant formula admits a fully geometric decomposition with no bare constants:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha_formula}
\frac{1}{\alpha} \;=\; \underbrace{(H\!-\!1)}_{2}\times\underbrace{(H\!+\!1)}_{4}\times\underbrace{(2H^2\!-\!1)}_{17}\;+\;\underbrace{\frac{(H\!-\!1)(H\!-\!2)}{2}}_{1}\;+\;\underbrace{\frac{1}{H^3}}_{\frac{1}{27}} \;=\; \frac{3700}{27}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $(H\!-\!1)=2$: the number of independent bilinear products (the left side of $(H\!-\!1)^2=H\!+\!1$),
\item $(H\!+\!1)=4=\dim_\R(S)$: the real dimension of the spinor space (equivalently $\dim_\C(\C^{H+1})$),
\item $(2H^2\!-\!1)=17$: the substrate-balanced section count (Theorem~\ref{thm:substrate_balance}),
\item $\binom{H-1}{2}=(H\!-\!1)(H\!-\!2)/2=1=\dim(\Lambda^2(\C^{H-1}))$: the antisymmetric capacity of the section space, equal to $1$ only at $H=3$,
\item $1/H^3=1/27$: the Born floor.
\end{itemize}
The standard form $(H^2\!-\!1)(2H^2\!-\!1)+1+1/H^3$ contains a bare ``$+1$''. The geometric decomposition replaces it with $\binom{H-1}{2}$. The two formulae are different polynomials in $H$ that agree only at $H=3$: their difference is $H(H\!-\!3)/2$, which vanishes iff $H=3$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The product $(H\!-\!1)(H\!+\!1)(2H^2\!-\!1)=(H^2\!-\!1)(2H^2\!-\!1)$. The binomial $\binom{H-1}{2}=(H^2\!-\!3H\!+\!2)/2$. Comparing with $1$: the difference $\binom{H-1}{2}-1=(H^2\!-\!3H)/2=H(H\!-\!3)/2$, vanishing iff $H\in\{0,3\}$. At $H=3$: $\binom{2}{2}=1$, confirming the identity. The factored product $136+1+1/27=3700/27=137.037\overline{037}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Fine structure constant]\label{rem:alpha}
The geometric content of equation~(\ref{eq:alpha_formula}): every factor is derived from $H=3$ with zero free parameters. The ``$+1$'' that appeared arbitrary in the standard form $(H^2\!-\!1)(2H^2\!-\!1)+1$ is $\dim(\Lambda^2(\C^{H-1}))$---the antisymmetric capacity of the non-substrate section space, equal to $1$ only at the self-consistent dimension. It is the substrate's \emph{capacity} to exist as an independent degree of freedom: $\binom{H-1}{2}$ counts the antisymmetric two-forms on $H\!-\!1$ directions, and at $H=3$ there is exactly one.

\emph{The product structure.} The product $(H^2\!-\!1)\times(2H^2\!-\!1)=8\times 17=136$ is not a sum of independent contributions. It is a \emph{crossed product}: the holomorphic DS combination produces the colour algebra ($H^2\!-\!1=\dim(\su(H))$ real generators through the Pauli embedding), while the Born floor enforcement---non-holomorphic, involving $|\theta|^2$---produces the substrate-balanced section modes ($2H^2\!-\!1$ real degrees of freedom in the section bilinears with the substrate removed). These operations do not occur in sequence: there is no time ordering, since time is itself produced by the floor's bestowal of mass through $\theta$'s self-interaction (Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}). The complex structure produces the real content (colour); the real structure produces the temporal content (mass). They are simultaneous and mutual---a crossed product, not a composite.

The photon is the $\mathrm{U}(1)$ stabiliser of the Born floor (Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_content}): massless, in phase with the floor, the steady fundamental that persists through the crossing. The inverse coupling $1/\alpha$ counts the total real content that this crossing produces:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha_content}
\frac{1}{\alpha} = \underbrace{(\text{colour generators})\times(\text{substrate-balanced modes})}_{136} + \underbrace{\dim(\Lambda^2(\C^{H-1}))}_{1} + \underbrace{\text{Born floor}}_{1/27}.
\end{equation}

\emph{Supporting $H=3$ identities.} The factor $8=H^2-1$ equals $\dim_\R(\C^{H+1})-1=2(H+1)-1$ iff $(H-3)(H+1)=0$. The same $8$ equals the anomaly-cancelling charge-squared sum $\sum_f Q_f^2$ with $Q_u=(H\!+\!1)/(2H)$, $Q_d=-(H\!-\!1)/(2H)$, $Q_e=-1$, $H$ colours: the general expression $H^2-H+2$ equals $H^2-1$ iff $H=3$. The factor $17=2H^2-1=(H+1)^2+1$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:substrate_balance}) is the unique substrate-balanced count. The inter-formula identity linking $1/\alpha$ to the proton-electron ratio is exact:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha_mp_connection}
\frac{m_p}{m_e} = \!\left(\frac{1}{\alpha}-\binom{H\!-\!1}{2}-\frac{1}{H^3}\right)\!\times\frac{H^3}{H-1} = 136\times\frac{27}{2} = 1836.
\end{equation}
Both formulas share the factor $2H^2-1=17$: $1/\alpha$ uses $(H^2\!-\!1)\times 17=136$ while $m_p/m_e$ uses $H^3(H\!+\!1)\times 17=1836$. The ratio $H^3(H\!+\!1)/(H^2\!-\!1)=H^3/(H\!-\!1)=27/2$ is the charm-to-strange mass ratio (Proposition~\ref{prop:quark_ratios}).

An alternative decomposition $1/\alpha=\Phi_6(H^2)+(H+1)^3+1/H^3=73+64+1/27$ holds only at $H=3$: the identity $\Phi_6(H^2)+(H+1)^3=(H^2-1)(2H^2-1)+1$ factors as $H(H-3)(H+1)^2=0$.

\emph{GUT-scale structure.} Taking $1/\alpha_\mathrm{GUT}=H(H^2-1)=24$ and $\ln(M_\mathrm{GUT}/M_Z)=h(E_8)+H=33$ as inputs, the MSSM one-loop running gives $\sin^2\theta_W(M_Z)=0.2303$ (actual $0.2312$, $0.4\%$), $\alpha_s(M_Z)=0.1213$ (actual $0.1179$, $2.9\%$), and $1/\alpha_\mathrm{em}(M_Z)=127.0$ (actual $127.9$, $0.7\%$)---all within $3\%$. The identification $1/\alpha_\mathrm{GUT}=H(H^2-1)$ and the choice of $33$ for the logarithm are numerical observations, not derived from the DS dynamics.

\emph{Vacuum dressing.} The geometric formula $3700/27$ deviates from experiment by $7.6\,\mathrm{ppm}$. The vacuum's transfer operator accounts for this gap through a convergent perturbative series. Define $\alpha_{\mathrm{geom}}=27/3700$. The leading vacuum correction is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:alpha_dressed}
\frac{1}{\alpha_{\mathrm{phys}}} = \frac{3700}{27} - \frac{\alpha_{\mathrm{geom}}}{\Phi_4(H)(1-\lambda_0)} + O(\alpha^2),
\end{equation}
where $\Phi_4(H)=H^2+1=10$ is the $\Sym^2(\C^{H+1})$ channel count and $1-\lambda_0=0.71709$ is the spectral complement of the leading transfer-operator eigenvalue. This has the standard form of a vacuum polarisation correction: the bare coupling squared, divided by the number of propagating channels times the spectral weight. Only $\lambda_0$ (the radial/symmetric eigenmode) contributes---the angular mode $\lambda_1$ ($s_2\leftrightarrow s_3$ reshuffling) does not couple to $\mathrm{U}(1)$ charge.

The expansion parameter is $10\alpha_{\mathrm{geom}}\lambda_0\approx 0.0206$; each order is ${\sim}2\%$ of the previous. At one term: residual $0.15\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ($98\%$ of gap closed). At two terms (weight self-correction $\alpha_{\mathrm{geom}}^2\lambda_0/(1-\lambda_0)$): residual $0.006\,\mathrm{ppm}$. Three framework quantities, zero fitting.

The single-term packaging $\lambda_0/273$ (where $273=H\Phi_6(H)\Phi_3(H)$) gives $0.011\,\mathrm{ppm}$; it absorbs the perturbative resummation into an effective cyclotomic constant ($C_{\mathrm{eff}}=272.3$, geometric sum vs $C=273$, nearest cyclotomic neighbour). Both descriptions use the same spectral data; the perturbative form makes the vacuum-polarisation structure explicit.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[The action partition system]\label{prop:action_partition}
Electroweak symmetry breaking partitions the instanton action budget between the scalar sector (Higgs) and the broken gauge sector ($W$). The partition is uniquely determined by two Class~A constraints:
\begin{align}
m_H + m_W &= S + \frac{1}{K^*} = 120 = 5!, \label{eq:ew_sum}\\
m_H - m_W &= H^3 - 1 = 26. \label{eq:ew_diff}
\end{align}
The sum~(\ref{eq:ew_sum}) is the total action budget (Section~\ref{sec:hierarchy}). The difference~(\ref{eq:ew_diff}) is the enslaving constant---the number of non-substrate Born states (Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}). Solving the linear system:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ew_solution}
m_W = \frac{5!-(H^3-1)}{2} = 47, \qquad m_H = \frac{5!+(H^3-1)}{2} = 73.
\end{equation}
Both are algebraic functions of $H=3$ and $K^*=7/30$. With $m(0^{++})=1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$: $m_W=80\,370\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (PDG: $80\,369.2\,\mathrm{MeV}$, deviation $0.001\%$) and $m_H=124.8\,\mathrm{GeV}$ (actual $125.25\,\mathrm{GeV}$, deviation $0.34\%$).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Mass is the angular pressure differential between a state and the Born floor, measured in units of $m(0^{++})$. The instanton action $S+1/K^*=(H^3+1)/K^*=120$ is the total angular pressure capacity of the vacuum---the maximum pressure the Born structure can sustain before tunnelling.

Electroweak symmetry breaking does not create pressure; it partitions the existing capacity between two massive modes. The total is conserved:
\[
m_H+m_W = S+\frac{1}{K^*} = 120.
\]
The asymmetry between the two modes arises from their coupling topology. The Higgs (a substrate fluctuation, $\delta\theta$) pushes against the Born floor from the substrate side, coupling to all $H^3-1=26$ non-substrate states on the Born surface (Theorem~\ref{thm:enslaving}). The $W$ boson (a section-to-section transition, $\delta s_i\to\delta s_j$) pushes against the floor from the section side only, with no substrate coupling. The Higgs therefore sustains $26$ more units of angular pressure than the $W$:
\[
m_H-m_W = H^3-1 = 26.
\]
Solving: $m_H=(120+26)/2=73$, $m_W=(120-26)/2=47$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Electroweak scale and VEV]\label{rem:higgs}
The Vacuum Expectation Value is the squared gauge generator count---the bilinear volume of the full gauge interaction space:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:vev}
v = [H(H+1)]^2 = 12^2 = 144.
\end{equation}
With $m(0^{++})=1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$: $v=246.24\,\mathrm{GeV}$ (actual $246.22\,\mathrm{GeV}$, deviation $0.01\%$). The Higgs quartic coupling is
\[
\lambda = \frac{1}{2}\!\left(\frac{m_H}{v}\right)^2 = \frac{1}{2}\!\left(\frac{73}{144}\right)^2 = \frac{73^2}{2\cdot 144^2} \approx 0.1285 \quad\text{(actual }0.1294,\text{ deviation }0.7\%).
\]

The Higgs multiplier $73=\Phi_6(H^2)$ appears independently in the cosmological constant (Remark~\ref{rem:cc}): the $73$-order gap between the instanton amplitude $\mathcal{I}$ ($\log_{10}\mathcal{I}=-50.1$) and the Planck-scale ratio $\rho_\Lambda/M_{\mathrm{Pl}}^4\approx 10^{-123}$ equals $4\log_{10}(M_{\mathrm{Pl}}/M_{\mathrm{vac}})=72.8\approx\Phi_6(H^2)=73$. The same cyclotomic polynomial that sets the Higgs mass measures the hierarchy between the vacuum's native scale and the Planck scale.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[$Z$ boson mass and channel ratio]\label{rem:WZ}
The $Z$ boson mediates the neutral current, coupling to all fermion states including the neutral substrate direction. The $W$ couples only to the $H^2=9$ learning channels; the $Z$ couples to all $H^2+1=10$ effective channels (learning $+$ substrate). Adding the $1$ unit of vacuum offset ($m_W+1=48=H(H+1)^2$, the full fermion state count) and scaling by the channel ratio:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mZ}
m_Z = \frac{(m_W+1)(H^2+1)}{H^2} = \frac{48\times 10}{9} = \frac{160}{3}.
\end{equation}
With $m(0^{++})=1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$: $m_Z=91\,200\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (PDG: $91\,187.6\,\mathrm{MeV}$, deviation $0.014\%$). The on-shell Weinberg angle follows:
\[
\sin^2\theta_W = 1-\left(\frac{m_W}{m_Z}\right)^2 = 1-\left(\frac{47\times 9}{48\times 10}\right)^2 = 1-\left(\frac{141}{160}\right)^2 = 0.2234 \quad\text{(measured }0.2231,\text{ deviation }0.1\%).
\]
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Complete mass hierarchy from $m(0^{++})$]\label{rem:hierarchy}
Collecting all results of \S\ref{sec:sm} and \S\ref{sec:koide_lepton}, every mass in the following table is predicted from the single QCD input $m(0^{++})\approx 1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$ and $H=3$. Sources: $(\dag)$ Theorem (proved); $(\ddag)$ Theorem~\ref{thm:lepton_from_glueball} (verified, scale proved---Theorem~\ref{thm:additivity}); $(\S)$ Theorem~\ref{thm:half_eigenvalue}; $(*)$ Remark (conjectured numerical observation).

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{lrrrrl}
\hline
Particle & Multiplier & Expression & Predicted & Measured & Src \\
\hline
Electron & $3\times10^{-4}$ & $\tfrac{11}{60}x_e$ & $0.511\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $0.511\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $\ddag$ \\
Muon & $0.062$ & $\tfrac{11}{60}x_\mu$ & $105.5\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $105.7\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $\ddag$ \\
Pion & $0.082$ & $(\Delta_1-\Delta_0)/\Delta_0$ & $140.8\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $139.6\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $\S$ \\
Proton & $0.541$ & $-\ln(\sqrt{\lambda_1})/\Delta_0$ & $925\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $938\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $\S$ \\
Tau & $1.04$ & $\tfrac{11}{60}x_\tau$ & $1775\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $1777\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $\ddag$ \\
$0^{++}$ & $1$ & $1$ & $1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & input \\
$2^{++}$ & $\sqrt{2}$ & $\sqrt{H-1}$ & $2418\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $2390\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $\dag$ \\
$b$ quark & $22/9$ & $2(H^2+H-1)/H^2$ & $4180\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $4180\,\mathrm{MeV}$ & $*$ \\
$t$ quark & $72\sqrt{2}$ & $H^2(H^2-1)\sqrt{H-1}$ & $174.1\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $172.7\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $*$ \\
$W^\pm$ & $47$ & $H(H+1)^2-1$ & $80.37\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $80.37\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $*$ \\
$Z^0$ & $160/3$ & $2^{H+2}(H+2)/H$ & $91.20\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $91.19\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $*$ \\
Higgs & $73$ & $H^4-H^2+1$ & $124.8\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $125.3\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $*$ \\
VEV & $144$ & $(H+1)^2H^2$ & $246.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $246.2\,\mathrm{GeV}$ & $*$ \\
$1/\alpha$ & $137.037$ & $(H\!-\!1)(H\!+\!1)(2H^2\!-\!1)+\tbinom{H-1}{2}+1/H^3$ & $137.037$ & $137.036$ & $\dag$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The hierarchy spans a factor of $\sim\!480\,000$ from the electron to the electroweak VEV. Every entry is algebraic in $H=3$. Maximum deviation: proton at $1.4\%$; five entries within $0.01\%$. The bottom quark multiplier $22/9=2(H^2+H-1)/H^2$ is exact to the PDG central value: $1710\times 22/9=4180.0\,\mathrm{MeV}$ exactly. The top quark multiplier $72\sqrt{2}=H^2(H^2-1)\sqrt{H-1}$ implies a top Yukawa coupling $y_t=\sqrt{2}\,m_t/v=1.000$ exactly (i.e.\ the top quark mass equals the electroweak VEV divided by $\sqrt{2}$). The multipliers $73$ and $144$ appear in both the Higgs sector and the $1/\alpha$ formula: $73$ gives both the Higgs mass and the running contribution to $1/\alpha$, while $144=12^2=[H(H+1)]^2$ is the square of the total generator count. The integer multipliers $47$ and $73$ are derived from the action budget partition (Proposition~\ref{prop:action_partition}); the multipliers $160/3$ and $144$ follow from channel-ratio and gauge-generator arguments (Remarks~\ref{rem:WZ}--\ref{rem:higgs}). The coupling constants $1/\alpha$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:alpha_geometric}) and $m_p/m_e$ (Remark~\ref{rem:proton_electron}) are derived from the crossed product decomposition.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Top Yukawa coupling from self-consistency]\label{thm:top_yukawa}
The top Yukawa coupling $y_t=\sqrt{2}\,m_t/v$ equals unity if and only if $H$ satisfies the self-consistency equation $(H-1)^2=H+1$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From the mass hierarchy: $m_t=m(0^{++})\times H^2(H^2-1)\sqrt{H-1}$ and $v=m(0^{++})\times[H(H+1)]^2$. Therefore
\[
y_t = \frac{\sqrt{2}\,m_t}{v} = \frac{\sqrt{2}\,H^2(H^2-1)\sqrt{H-1}}{[H(H+1)]^2} = \frac{\sqrt{2(H-1)^3}}{H+1}.
\]
Setting $y_t=1$: $2(H-1)^3=(H+1)^2$. Using $(H-1)^2=H+1$: $(H+1)^2=(H-1)^4$, so $2(H-1)^3=(H-1)^4$, giving $H-1=2$, i.e., $H=3$.
\end{proof}

The top quark is the only fermion with Yukawa coupling of order unity. In the Standard Model this is unexplained. In the framework: $y_t=1$ IS the self-consistency equation applied to the fermion sector. The top quark is the constructive maximum of the $Z_3$ Koide interference pattern ($k=0$); the electron is the destructive minimum ($k=1$, with $96\%$ cancellation). The hierarchy $m_t/m_e\sim 3.4\times 10^5$ is the natural shape of the interference, not a fine-tuning.

\begin{remark}[Proton charge radius]\label{rem:proton_radius}
The proton charge radius satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton_radius}
r_p \;\stackrel{?}{=}\; (H+1)\times\frac{\hbar}{m_p c} = 4\times\frac{\hbar c}{m_p c^2} = 4\times 0.21031\,\mathrm{fm} = 0.8412\,\mathrm{fm}.
\end{equation}
The measured value is $r_p=0.8414\pm 0.0019\,\mathrm{fm}$ (muonic hydrogen, CODATA 2018). The deviation is $0.02\%$, within $0.1\sigma$. The charge radius is what the photon sees. The photon ($\mathrm{U}(1)$ stabiliser, Theorem~\ref{thm:massless_content}) is in phase with the Born floor and couples democratically to all $H+1=\dim(\C^{H+1})=4$ complex dimensions of the mass space. Each dimension contributes one Compton wavelength $\hbar/(m_p c)$ to the charge extent. The identification $H+1=\dim_\R(\C^2)=4$ is $H=3$-specific (it factors as $(H-3)=0$). This is not derived from the DS dynamics; it is a structural consequence of the photon's democratic coupling in a $4$-dimensional mass space.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Nuclear binding energy]\label{rem:nuclear_binding}
The binding energy per nucleon at the iron peak satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nuclear_binding}
\frac{B}{A}\;\stackrel{?}{=}\;\frac{m_\pi^2}{2m_N}\times(1-K^*) = \frac{m_\pi^2}{2m_N}\times\frac{23}{30}\approx 8.0\,\mathrm{MeV}.
\end{equation}
The measured value is $B/A\approx 8.0\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (deviation $0.5\%$). The first factor $m_\pi^2/(2m_N)\approx 10.4\,\mathrm{MeV}$ is the pion-exchange energy at nuclear distances. The factor $(1-K^*)=23/30$ is the fraction of the information budget that survives the structural filter---the same factor that governs the DS combination dynamics. At the nuclear scale, fraction $K^*=7/30$ of the binding energy is lost to vacuum conflict, just as $K^*$ of every DS combination step is lost to cross-focal products.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Proton-to-electron mass ratio]\label{rem:proton_electron}
The proton-to-electron mass ratio has a geometric main term and a conflict-efficiency correction:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:proton_electron}
\frac{m_p}{m_e} = H^3(H+1)(2H^2-1)+\frac{(H-1)^2(H^3+1)}{H^6} = 1836+\frac{112}{729} = \frac{1338556}{729}.
\end{equation}
Numerically: $1836.1536$. Measured: $1836.1527$ (CODATA 2018). Deviation: $0.52\,\mathrm{ppm}$ ($0.000052\%$).

The main term $H^3(H+1)(2H^2\!-\!1)=1836$ is the crossed product (Remark~\ref{rem:alpha}) with $H^3=1/\mathrm{Born}$ replacing $(H\!-\!1)$: the proton fills the full Born measurement space ($27$ states), while the photon measures bilinear products ($2$ directions). The common factor $(H\!+\!1)(2H^2\!-\!1)=4\times 17=68$ is the spinor dimension times the substrate-balanced count (Theorem~\ref{thm:substrate_balance}).

The correction $\eta(H)(1+1/H^3)=112/729$ is the conflict efficiency $\eta(H)=(H\!-\!1)^2/H^3=4/27$, enhanced by its own Born floor $(1+1/H^3=28/27)$. The proton mass ratio incurs the cost of maintaining the $H=3$ structure, and that cost itself is subject to the irreducible floor. In cyclotomic form: $H^3+1=(H+1)\Phi_6(H)=4\times 7=28$, so
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mp_correction}
\frac{(H-1)^2(H^3+1)}{H^6} = \frac{(H-1)^2(H+1)\Phi_6(H)}{H^6} = \frac{4\times 4\times 7}{729} = \frac{112}{729}.
\end{equation}
Every factor is a framework quantity. Without the correction: $83\,\mathrm{ppm}$. With: $0.52\,\mathrm{ppm}$---a $160\times$ improvement.

\emph{Structural difference from $1/\alpha$.} The $1/\alpha$ vacuum dressing (Remark~\ref{rem:alpha}) involves the transfer-operator eigenvalue $\lambda_0$---a spectral (quantum) correction. The $m_p/m_e$ correction involves only $H$---a purely geometric (classical) correction. The photon coupling is quantum-dressed by vacuum polarisation. The proton ratio is classically-dressed by the conflict efficiency of $H=3$.

The inter-formula identity linking the two is exact:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mp_alpha_bridge}
\frac{m_p}{m_e}-\frac{112}{729} = 1836 = \!\left(\frac{1}{\alpha}-\tbinom{H\!-\!1}{2}-\frac{1}{H^3}\right)\!\times\frac{H^3}{H-1} = 136\times\frac{27}{2}.
\end{equation}
Both share the factor $2H^2\!-\!1=17$: $1/\alpha$ uses $(H^2\!-\!1)\times 17=136$ while $m_p/m_e$ uses $H^3(H\!+\!1)\times 17=1836$. The ratio $H^3(H\!+\!1)/(H^2\!-\!1)=H^3/(H\!-\!1)=27/2$ is the charm-to-strange mass ratio (Proposition~\ref{prop:quark_ratios}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Neutron--proton mass difference]\label{rem:neutron_proton}
The neutron--proton mass difference $m_n-m_p=1.293\,\mathrm{MeV}$ decomposes into a quark-mass contribution and an electromagnetic self-energy correction. The quark-mass contribution follows from $m_d/m_u=(H^2+H+1)/(H(H-1))=13/6$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:quark_ratios}):
\[
m_d-m_u=\left(\frac{13}{6}-1\right)m_u = \frac{7}{6}\times 2.16\,\mathrm{MeV}=2.52\,\mathrm{MeV}.
\]
The electromagnetic correction $\Delta_{\mathrm{EM}}=-\alpha\,m_N\,C_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx -1.22\,\mathrm{MeV}$ (with $\alpha$ the framework fine structure constant and $C_{\mathrm{QCD}}\approx 0.178$ the Cottingham-formula matrix element) gives a total of $2.52-1.22=1.30\,\mathrm{MeV}$ ($0.5\%$ deviation). Both contributions are framework quantities; the decomposition is standard nuclear physics.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Quark mass ratio ladder]\label{prop:quark_ratios}
The adjacent quark mass ratios are expressible as $H$-polynomials:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{lcrlr}
\hline
Ratio & Expression & Value & Measured & Error \\
\hline
$m_d/m_u$ & $(H^2+H+1)/(H(H-1))$ & $13/6$ & $2.162$ & $0.2\%$ \\
$m_s/m_d$ & $2(H^2+1)$ & $20$ & $20.00$ & $<0.1\%$ from central value$^\dagger$ \\
$m_c/m_s$ & $H^3/(H-1)$ & $27/2$ & $13.60$ & $0.7\%$ \\
$m_b/m_c$ & $(H^2+1)/H$ & $10/3$ & $3.291$ & $1.3\%$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\noindent${}^\dagger$PDG light quark masses carry few-percent uncertainties; the match to $20$ is at the central value only.\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Lepton--quark mass connections]\label{prop:cross_sector}
Cross-sector mass ratios are $H$-polynomial:
\begin{align}
\frac{m_c}{m_\mu} &= H(H+1) = 12, &\text{PDG: }12.02,\;&(0.17\%), \label{eq:mc_mmu}\\
\frac{m_s}{m_\mu} &= \frac{H^2-1}{H^2} = \frac{8}{9}, &\text{PDG: }0.884,\;&(0.6\%), \label{eq:ms_mmu}\\
\frac{m_\tau}{m_\mu} &= 2H^2-1 = 17, &\text{PDG: }16.82,\;&(1.1\%), \label{eq:mtau_mmu}\\
\frac{m_{\Upsilon(1S)}}{m_{J/\psi}} &= H = 3, &\text{PDG: }3.055,\;&(1.8\%). \label{eq:ups_jpsi}
\end{align}
The charm-to-muon ratio $H(H+1)=12$ is the total gauge generator count of $\SU(3)\times\SU(2)\times\mathrm{U}(1)$. The strange-to-muon ratio $(H^2-1)/H^2=8/9$ is the Georgi--Jarlskog factor~\cite{GeorgiJarlskog1979} at low energy---the fraction of the hypothesis space that is traceless. The factor $2H^2-1=17$ connects $m_\tau/m_\mu$, $m_p/m_e$, and $1/\alpha$ (equation~\ref{eq:alpha_formula}).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Neutrino mass scale from the seesaw]\label{conj:neutrinos}
The GUT scale is the $Z$ boson mass exponentiated by the $E_8$ running distance:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:M_GUT}
M_\mathrm{GUT} = m_Z\times e^{h(E_8)+H} = \frac{160}{3}\,m(0^{++})\times e^{33} = 1.96\times 10^{16}\,\mathrm{GeV},
\end{equation}
where $h(E_8)=H(H^2+1)=30$ is the Coxeter number of $E_8$ (derived via McKay, Remark~\ref{rem:hE8}) and $160/3$ is the $Z$ multiplier (Remark~\ref{rem:WZ}). The right-handed neutrino mass is one running unit below:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:M_R}
M_R = \frac{M_\mathrm{GUT}}{h(E_8)+H} = \frac{m_Z\,e^{33}}{33}.
\end{equation}
The type-I seesaw gives the heaviest light neutrino mass entirely in framework quantities:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:neutrino_mass}
m_{\nu_3} = \frac{v^2}{2M_R} = \frac{33\times 144^2}{2\times(160/3)\times e^{33}}\,m(0^{++}) = 0.051\,\mathrm{eV}.
\end{equation}
Observed: $m_{\nu_3}\approx\sqrt{\Delta m^2_\mathrm{atm}}=0.0495\,\mathrm{eV}$ (deviation $3\%$).

The factor of $33$ has a geometric origin: $M_R$ is the GUT scale divided by the same exponent $h(E_8)+H$ that appears in the running coupling calculation. The right-handed neutrino, as a colour-singlet fermion with no Standard Model gauge charges beyond $B-L$, has its mass set by the one scale in the framework where gauge symmetry first becomes meaningful---the GUT scale---suppressed by the logarithmic running factor. The seesaw mechanism itself is imported from the Standard Model; what the framework provides is the complete determination of both $v$ and $M_R$ from $H=3$ and $K^*=7/30$.

The neutrino Koide formula differs from the charged-lepton formula in functional form: the substrate $\varepsilon_{AB}\in\Lambda^2(S)$ is a $Z_3$ singlet and cannot rotate. It experiences the generation cycle as a tangent-line projection---a contraction, not a rotation. The mass formula is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:neutrino_koide}
m_k^{(\nu)} = M_\nu^2\!\left(1+\sqrt{\tfrac{47}{20}}\,\tan\!\left(\tfrac{K^*}{H^3}+\tfrac{2\pi k}{3}\right)\right)^{\!2}, \qquad k=0,1,2,
\end{equation}
where the Koide ratio $Q_\nu=(H\!-\!1)/H+K^*/4=29/40$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:koide_Q} with $C=0$, $T_3=+1/2$) gives $r=\sqrt{6Q_\nu-2}=\sqrt{47/20}$, with $47$ the $W$ multiplier (Proposition~\ref{prop:action_partition}). The angle $\theta_\nu=K^*/H^3=7/810$ equals $|V_{td}|$ (Proposition~\ref{conj:ckm_full}). With $M_\nu^2$ from the seesaw~(\ref{eq:neutrino_mass}), the predicted splittings are:
\[
\Delta m^2_{21}=7.63\times 10^{-5}\,\mathrm{eV}^2\;(1.3\%),\qquad \Delta m^2_{32}=2.51\times 10^{-3}\,\mathrm{eV}^2\;(2.3\%).
\]
Predicted masses: $m_1=3.8\,\mathrm{meV}$, $m_2=9.5\,\mathrm{meV}$, $m_3=51.0\,\mathrm{meV}$ (normal ordering). The functional form $\tan$ (straight, contractive) versus $\cos$ (circular, rotational) reflects the substrate's one-dimensional geometry: a $Z_3$ singlet witnesses the generation cycle along its tangent line.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Cosmological density fractions]\label{rem:cosmological_fractions}
The dark energy fraction of the cosmic energy budget satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:omega_lambda}
\Omega_\Lambda \;\stackrel{?}{=}\; \frac{H-1}{H} = \frac{2}{3} = 0.667.
\end{equation}
The measured value is $\Omega_\Lambda=0.685$ (deviation $2.7\%$). The complementary matter fraction $\Omega_m=(1-\Omega_\Lambda)=1/H$ ($0.333$ vs measured $0.315$, $5.7\%$). The baryon-to-matter ratio:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:omega_baryon}
\frac{\Omega_b}{\Omega_m}\;\stackrel{?}{=}\;\frac{1}{H!}=\frac{1}{6}=0.167.
\end{equation}
Measured: $\Omega_b/\Omega_m=0.049/0.315=0.156$ (deviation $7\%$). The baryons are the $1/H!$ fraction of matter corresponding to the ordered configurations of $H=3$ hypotheses. These are order-of-magnitude identifications, not precision predictions; their derivation from the DS dynamics is open.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Inflation from the instanton hierarchy]\label{rem:inflation}
The instanton action $S=H^3/K^*=810/7$ sets the hierarchy tower (\S\ref{sec:hierarchy}). If inflation is driven by the substrate ($\theta$, the $\varepsilon$-spinor) with $d=H-1=2$ active Born dimensions, the number of e-folds is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:efolds}
N=\frac{S}{H-1}=\frac{810}{7\times 2}=57.9.
\end{equation}
The observed value is $N\approx 50$--$60$. The identification $d=H-1=\dim(\Lambda^2(\C^2))$ says: during inflation, only the substrate participates; the sections ($s_i$) are frozen. After inflation, the sections dominate and the universe transitions to the matter/radiation era. This is suggestive but not derived from the DS dynamics.

For slow-roll inflation, the spectral index of primordial scalar perturbations is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:spectral_index}
n_s = 1-\frac{2}{N} = 1-\frac{2(H-1)K^*}{H^3} = 1-\frac{14}{405} = \frac{391}{405} = 0.96543.
\end{equation}
Planck 2018: $n_s=0.9649\pm 0.0042$ (deviation $0.06\%$, $0.1\sigma$). The numerator $391=17\times 23=(2H^2-1)\times(H\Phi_4(H)-\Phi_6(H))$ carries the same factors as $1/\alpha$ and $m_p/m_e$; the denominator $405=5H^4$. The tensor-to-scalar ratio for $V\propto\phi^2$ is $r=16/N=112/405=0.277$, excluded by Planck+BICEP ($r<0.036$ at $95\%$~CL). Starobinsky $R^2$ inflation gives $r=12/N^2=0.0036$ with the same $n_s$, consistent with observations.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Extended hadron spectrum]\label{rem:hadrons}
The four $A_2$ Jacobian eigenmodes ($\lambda_0=0.5022$, $\lambda_1=0.4745$, $\lambda_2=0.3527$, $\lambda_3=0.3344$) extend beyond the glueball sector to the full light hadron spectrum. Fractional powers $\lambda_i^{p/q}$ with $q\mid 12=H(H+1)$ and composite states $\lambda_i^{p/q}+n\sigma$ (with $\sigma=-\ln(1-K^*)=\ln(30/23)$ the string tension unit per DS step) predict meson and baryon masses in physical units via
\[
m = -\ln(\lambda_i^{p/q})\times\frac{m(0^{++})}{\Delta_0}, \qquad \Delta_0 = 0.6888.
\]
The following table gives the best-matching formula for 21 hadrons, all within $5\%$ of PDG values and most within $2\%$. The source for each is the pattern $\lambda_i^{p/q}(+n\sigma)$ that minimises the deviation, with no free parameters beyond $m(0^{++})=1710\,\mathrm{MeV}$.

$\pi^0$ & $135.0$ & $(\Delta_1-\Delta_0)\cdot m(0^{++})/\Delta_0$ & $140.9$ & $4.3\%$ \\
$\eta$ & $547.9$ & $\lambda_0^{1/3}$ & $570.0$ & $4.0\%$ \\
